    Policy Framework
M-1:              MULTIMODAL TRANSPORTATION
                  CHOICES
Goal M-1
Expanded multimodal transportation choices that improve the
ability to travel efficiently and safely throughout the city and region.
  MULTIMODAL TRANSPORTATION POLICIES
M-1.1           Multimodal Options. Establish an interconnected transportation network
                that offers safe and convenient mobility options including adequate
                streets, transit services, pedestrian walkways, bike routes, equestrian
                facilities, commercial rail connections, and aviation services. (RDR, MP,
                IGC, JP, NR-IP5)
M-1.2           Range of Users. Ensure that the transportation network meets the needs
                of a variety of users eliminating barriers, where feasible, to allow access
                by people of all abilities. (RDR, MP, IGC, JP)
M-1.3           Complete Streets. Design and construct both new and reconstructed
                streets with adequate rights-of way and facilities to support the full range
                of locally available travel modes, compliant with the California Complete
                Streets Act (AB 1358). (RDR, MP, IGC, JP)
                                                                        MOBILITY                        M-9

                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
COMPLETE STREETS
                                 Assembly Bill 1358, also known as the California Complete Streets Act of 2008, requires cities
                                 and counties to include “complete streets” policies in their general plans. Complete streets are
                                 designed and operated to enable safe access for all users including motorists, bicyclists,
                                 pedestrians, and public transit riders of all ages and abilities. Typical components of complete
                                 streets may include sidewalks, bike lanes, special bus lanes, comfortable and accessible transit
                                 stops, frequent crossing opportunities, median islands, accessible pedestrian signals, curb bulb-
                                 outs, and similar. Such components can be incorporated into the design of new streets, as well
                                 improvements to existing roadways.
Also See Land Use & Community M-1.4         Smart Growth. Integrate transportation and land use decisions to
                  Form Element              enhance opportunities for development that is compact, walkable and
                                            transit friendly. (RDR, JP, NR-IP5)
                               M-1.5        Multimodal Access. Promote the provision of multimodal access to
                                            activity centers, such as commercial and employment uses, Downtown,
                                            higher density and mixed use projects, schools, and parks. (RDR, MP, JP)
                               M-1.6        Consider all Users of Transportation System. Use multi-modal evaluation
                                            methods to ensure that projects do not result in worsening facilities or
                                            service for transit, bicyclists, and pedestrians. (MP, OFB, M-IP1)
                               M-2: VEHICULAR TRAVEL
                               Goal M-2
                               An interconnected roadway/highway system that ensures the safe
                               and efficient movement of people, goods, and services on multiple
                               routes by multiple modes.
                                ROADWAY & HIGHWAY SYSTEM POLICIES
                               M-2.1        Roadway Plan. Plan, design, and regulate roadways in accordance with
                                            the General Plan Circulation Diagram and City’s Roadway
                                            Classifications. (RDR, MP, EV-IP1)
                               M-2.2        Grid Network. Provide for a modified grid network of streets that
                                            promotes connectivity and walkability. (RDR, MP)
                               M-2.3        System Completion. Ensure completion of the roadway system through
                                            the elimination of substandard width segments and construction of
                                            missing links. (RDR, MP, M-IP2)
                               M-2.4        North County Corridor. Continue participation in the planning,
                                            preservation of right-of-way, and ultimate implementation of the North
                                            County Corridor. (IGC)
                           M-10                    MOBILITY

                                                 City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
M-2.5 Relinquishment. Coordinate with Caltrans on the relinquishment of SR
      108 within Oakdale to the City. (IGC, M-IP2)
 ROADWAY LEVEL OF SERVICE POLICIES
M-2.6 Level of Service (LOS) Standard. Maintain operations on most roadway
      segments and intersections in the City at Level of Service D or better at
      peak travel times. Allow reduced LOS standards of E or F on the
      following roadways:
              F Street (SR 108): Willowood Drive to Yosemite Avenue (LOS F)
              Yosemite Avenue (SR 120): Stanislaus River Bridge to F Street (LOS F)
              Yosemite Avenue: F Street to Southern City Limit (LOS E)
      Additional exceptions to the LOS D standard may be approved when
      determined by the City Council that: (1) the improvements necessary to
      maintain LOS D or better would be infeasible and/or conflict with the
      achievement of other community goals; and (2) provisions are made to
      improve other parts of the citywide transportation network in order to
      increase system-wide roadway capacity and/or enhance non-vehicular
      travel modes. (RDR, MP, M-IP1)
        LEVEL-OF-SERVICE
        The primary method used to analyze the performance of a roadway facility is level of
        service (LOS). LOS ranges from A through F, which represents driving conditions from
        least congested to most congested, respectively. The LOS grades for roadway types and
        facilities are generally defined as follows:
               LOS A represents free flow travel for vehicles.
               LOS B represents stable flow, but the presence of other users in the traffic stream
                begins to be noticeable.
               LOS C continues to represent stable flow, but interactions with others in the traffic
                stream significantly increases.
               LOS D represents high-density, stable flow, but approaching unstable conditions.
               LOS E represents unstable operating conditions at or near the capacity level where
                maneuverability is severely limited.
               LOS F defines forced traffic flow. Roadway volumes exceed the maximum capacity
                for the particular roadway classification.
                                                                 MOBILITY                          M-11

                                     City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                      ROADWAY IMPROVEMENT POLICIES
                                     M-2.7     Innovative Solutions. Promote effective, efficient, and innovative
                                               transportation solutions that reduce reliance on physical roadway
                                               improvements where appropriate. (RDR, MP)
                                     M-2.8     Improvement Standards. Maintain the City’s Standard Specifications for
                                               transportation rights-of-way and improvements, and update them on a
                                               regular basis as appropriate. Ensure that the City’s Standard
                                               Specifications provide flexibility and reflect the need to accommodate the
                                               full range of locally available travel modes. (RDR)
Also See City of Oakdale Climate     M-2.9     Electric Vehicles. Explore opportunities to accommodate electric vehicles
 Action Plan for additional GHG                (including golf carts and neighborhood electric vehicles) within the City’s
     emission reduction measures               transportation network, and encourage specialized parking and
        related to transportation.             charging/fueling stations. (M-IP3)
                                     M-2.10    Timing of Improvements. Provide identified transportation improvements
                                               in a timely manner to meet the needs of the community. (RDR, MP)
                                      NEW DEVELOPMENT POLICIES
                                     M-2.11    Traffic Studies. Require the preparation of site specific traffic studies for
                                               new development proposals that are determined by the City to have the
                                               potential to impact traffic. (RDR)
                                     M-2.12    Mitigation of Impacts. Require new development to construct, dedicate
                                               and/or pay its fair-share contribution to local and regional transportation
                                               improvements, including construction of on-site streets and mitigation of
                                               impacts upon existing and future roads through a variety of mechanisms
                                               such as the City’s Capital Facilities Fee and Community Facility Districts.
                                               (RDR, MP)
                                     M-2.13    Rights-of-Way Preservation. Preserve needed rights-of-way through
                                               dedication or acquisition as properties adjacent to transportation routes
                                               develop. (RDR, MP)
                                      TRAFFIC CONTROL POLICIES
                                     M-2.14    Traffic Control Strategies. Promote signal coordination along
                                               expressways and major arterials to effectively serve large traffic
                                               demands, and continue to work with Caltrans to implement traffic control
                                               strategies that will improve the level of service on the City’s street system.
                                               (MP, IGC, M-IP2)
                                     M-2.15    Intelligent Transportation Systems. Evaluate and implement cost effective
                                               intelligent transportation systems (such as signal coordination, centralized
                                               traffic control, and real-time travel information) to manage traffic flows.
                                               (MP, M-IP2)
                                 M-12                 MOBILITY

                                                   City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
M-2.16   Alternative Traffic Controls. Encourage the use of traffic controls that can
         add character and create opportunities for improved aesthetics (such as
         roundabouts and traffic circles) while effectively managing traffic.
         (RDR, MP)
 TRAFFIC CALMING POLICIES
M-2.17   Neighborhood Traffic Management. Incorporate traffic calming
         techniques as needed to reduce vehicle speeds, minimize neighborhood
         intrusion by through traffic, and promote safe and pleasant
         neighborhoods. (RDR)
M-2.18   Pedestrian Areas. Provide for narrower streets, appropriate curb radii,
         bulb-outs, enhanced crosswalks and similar techniques in areas of high
         pedestrian activity. (RDR, MP)
           TRAFFIC CALMING
           Traffic calming attempts to alter the behavior of motorists on a street or street
           network. It involves changes in street alignment, installation of barriers, and other
           physical measures to reduce traffic speeds and/or cut-through volumes, in the
           interest of street safety, livability, and other public purposes. Common traffic
           calming techniques include: landscaped curb bulb-outs to reduce the distance
           required for a pedestrian to cross a roadway; narrow streets; street islands and
           marked, signalized crossings to enhance pedestrian safety; street trees; speed
           humps; raised intersections; textured paving; traffic circles and roundabouts; half
           closures; diverters; and similar.
 PARKING POLICIES
M-2.19   Sufficient Parking. Ensure that sufficient and convenient on-street and off-
         street parking is provided for all uses. Consider potential reductions in
         off-street parking requirements based upon opportunities for shared
         parking, availability of on-street parking, and proximity to transit and
         other alternative modes of travel. (RDR)
M-2.20   Shared Parking. Support shared parking opportunities for uses with
         varied peak parking periods. (RDR)
M-2.21   On-street Parking. Maximize on-street parking in Downtown and other
         areas of high pedestrian activity. Minimize curb cuts to protect on-street
         parking spaces. (RDR)
M-2.22   Park and Ride Lots. Provide parking lots at strategic locations to facilitate
         Ride Share and transit connections. (RDR, MP, M-IP2)

Also See City of Oakdale Climate M-2.23       Large Employer TDM Program. Require major employers (100
 Action Plan for additional GHG               employees or more) to develop and implement Transportation Demand
     emission reduction measures              Management (TDM) programs and facilities (such as flexible working
         related to transportation.           hours, telecommuting, preferential parking for carpools/vanpools, high
                                              occupancy company-sponsored vehicles, ride-sharing programs, transit
                                              subsidies, and bicycle facilities) to lessen peak-hour commuter traffic.
                                              (RDR, M-IP2, NR-IP5)
      Also See Natural Resources M-2.24       City TDM Program. Establish a TDM program for City employees to
                           Element            promote carpooling and alternative modes of transportation. (M-IP4,
                                              NR-IP5)
                                               TRANSPORTATION DEMAND MANAGEMENT
                                               Transportation Demand Management (TDM) is a mix of measures promoting
                                               alternatives to the single occupant vehicle for employment related trips. TDM is
                                               intended to maximize the use of existing transportation infrastructure by influencing
                                               the time, route or mode selected for a given trip. TDM programs reduce vehicle
                                               miles traveled, parking demand, air quality impacts, and greenhouse gas
                                               emissions. Typical TDM measures may include employer promotion of and/or
                                               incentives for carpooling, vanpooling, transit use, walking, bicycling,
                                               telecommuting, alternative work schedules, and similar.
                                    M-3:        BICYCLISTS, PEDESTRIANS &
                                                EQUESTRIANS
                                    Goal M-3
                                    Enhanced bicycle, pedestrian and equestrian facilities that are
                                    accessible, safe, and convenient.
                                     BICYCLE & PEDESTRIAN POLICIES
                                    M-3.1     Bicycle and Pedestrian Master Plan. Implement and maintain the City’s
                                              Bicycle and Pedestrian Master Plan to guide the systematic planning,
                                              design, funding and construction of new and enhanced bicycle and
                                              pedestrian facilities. (MP, IGC, JP, M-IP2, NR-IP5)
                                M-14                 MOBILITY

                                         City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                   BICYCLE NETWORK
                                  Oakdale’s Bicycle and Pedestrian Master Plan addresses the following classifications of
                                  bikeways:
                                       Class I Bikeway (Bicycle Path) – Provides a completely separate right-of-way and is
                                        designated for the exclusive use of bicycles and pedestrians with vehicle and pedestrian
                                        cross-flow minimized. Particularly suited for young, less experienced and recreational
                                        cyclists.
                                       Class II Bikeway (Bicycle Lane) – Provides a restricted right-of-way and is designated for
                                        the use of bicycles with a striped lane on a street or highway. Vehicle and pedestrian
                                        cross-flow are permitted. This is the most common bikeway type in the City.
                                       Class III Bikeway (Bicycle Route) – Provides for a right-of-way designated by signs and/or
                                        pavement markings for shared use with pedestrians and motor vehicles. Typically
                                        designated on local, low-speed streets.
M-3.2 Cohesive Network. Provide a continuous bicycle and pedestrian

      network that links neighborhoods, parks, schools, commercial

      development, major employers and other frequently visited destinations.

      create recreational opportunities. (RDR, MP, NR-IP5)

                                   City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
    Also See Community Services M-3.10       Safe Routes to Schools. Work with the School District to support “safe
                          Element            routes to schools” programming that encourages children to walk and
                                             bicycle to school in a safe environment. (IGC, M-IP2)
                                               SAFE ROUTES TO SCHOOL
                                               Safe Routes to School (SRTS) programs are efforts by parents, schools, community
                                               leaders and local/state agencies to improve the health and well-being of children
                                               by enabling and encouraging them to walk and bicycle to school. SRTS programs
                                               examine conditions around schools and conduct projects and other activities to
                                               improve safety and accessibility, and reduce traffic and air pollution in the vicinity
                                               of schools. These programs also address the safety concerns of parents by
                                               encouraging greater enforcement of traffic laws, educating the public, and
                                               exploring ways to create safer routes to school from an early age. SRTS programs
                                               help make bicycling and walking to school safer and more appealing
                                               transportation choices thus encouraging a healthy and active lifestyle.
                                   M-3.11    Maintenance. Monitor and oversee the repair of sidewalks and paths
                                             that impede pedestrian and bicycle travel, and maintain the pedestrian
                                             and bicycle network in a manner that facilitates accessibility. (MP, OFB)
                                    EQUESTRIAN POLICIES
                                   M-3.12    Equestrian Facilities. Coordinate with local equestrian interests and the
                                             County to identify opportunities and funding sources for the development
                                             of equestrian trails and trailhead facilities. (IGC, OFB, M-IP5)

M-5.4     Rail. Work with railroad operators to facilitate the transport of goods by
          rail through the City when compatible with City traffic flows, adjacent
          uses and other community goals. (JP)
M-5.5     Grade Separations. Consider pursuing grade separations for at-grade
          railroad crossings within the City. (MP, JP, M-IP2)

OAKDALE 2030 GENERAL PLAN
PUBLIC FACILITIES

                                              City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                             Public Facilities
The Public Facilities Element establishes policies and standards for the planning and
provision of water, wastewater, storm drainage, solid waste, energy and
telecommunications services and infrastructure within the City of Oakdale. The intent
is to ensure adequate and efficient infrastructure to serve existing and future
residents and businesses, and to maximize valuable resources.
     Our public facilities vision includes…
       Reliable, cost-effective and sustainable utilities and infrastructure
                                                                                      CONTENTS
       Adequate capital facilities programs                                          Context
       Conservation of renewable resources                                           Policy Framework
                                                                                      PF-1    Water
                                                                                      PF-2    Wastewater
                                                                                      PF-3    Storm Drainage
                                                                                      PF-4    Solid Waste
                                                                                      PF-5    Energy
                                                                                      PF-6    Telecommunications
                                                    PUBLIC FACILITIES                PF-1

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
      Context
    The ability to deliver and maintain sufficient infrastructure contributes to Oakdale’s
    quality of life and level of attractiveness to economic growth and investment. The
    provision of infrastructure can influence the amount, type, intensity, pattern and
    quality of growth in the community. Infrastructure services in Oakdale are supplied
    by a combination of City and outside agencies:
       Water - The City of Oakdale provides water service within the City limits, and
        the Oakdale Irrigation District (OID) provides rural water service outside the City
        limits. The source of potable water for the City is exclusively groundwater,
        extracted from the Modesto Groundwater Subbasin. Water users that are not
        connected to a public water system utilize private wells, typically serving
        individual properties. Groundwater in the Oakdale area is known for its high
        quality, making treatment to comply with drinking water regulations unnecessary.
        The total volume of water supply projected and accounted for within the City’s
        Urban Water Management Plan is sufficient to meet the demands of the 2030
        General Plan. As a result, there are no immediate plans for use of surface water
        for potable water supply. The City of Oakdale could, however, be a possible
        future user of the New Melones Reservoir surface water, depending on escalating
        future demands and/or diminishing groundwater quality or quantity. Existing
        groundwater wells and water tanks are shown in Figure PF-1.
        The City developed the water-related goals and policies in coordination with all
        district and city agencies that have developed, served, controlled, managed, or
        conserved water of any type for any purpose in Oakdale.
PF-2                  PUBLIC FACILITIES

                                                  City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
   Wastewater - The City of Oakdale wastewater system provides service within
    the City limits. Some older properties within the City boundaries and areas
    outside of the City utilize septic systems. The Oakdale wastewater treatment
    plant (WWTP) is located on the north side of the Stanislaus River, as shown in
    Figure PF-1. This plant has been upgraded to provide tertiary treatment
    capability. Treated effluent may be reused for Reclaimed Water for Beneficial
    Reuse (RWBR) should distribution systems ultimately be developed. Existing sewer
    lift stations in the City are also shown in Figure PF-1. Future expansion of the
    City’s WWTP may require upgrades to existing transmission pipes and/or the
    installation of additional lift stations and force mains. A second treatment plant in
    the southern portion of the City, or decentralized wastewater treatment, may be
    considered.
    Storm Drainage - The City of Oakdale provides storm drainage within the City
     limits. Oakdale’s storm waters are either: 1) conveyed directly to the Stanislaus
     River through various pipe networks; or 2) collected and allowed to percolate into
     the ground through detention and retention basins, drywells, or French drain
     piping systems. Existing stormwater drainage basins in the City are shown in
     Figure PF-1. The City operates under a National Pollution Discharge Elimination
     System (NPDES) permit. Future legislation may require more stringent water
     quality standards and discharge regulations, possibly necessitating additional
     storage or treatment facilities.
    Solid Waste - Solid waste generated in the City of Oakdale is collected by
     Gilton Solid Waste Management. The City’s municipal solid waste is delivered
     to the Gilton Resource Recovery/Transfer Facility (GRR); a State permitted solid
     waste facility that provides a full range of transfer and diversion services. A
     majority of the City’s municipal solid waste delivered to GRR that is not diverted is
     sent to a landfill, with the bulk going to Forward Landfill in Manteca and a small
     portion going to Fink Road Landfill near Crows Landing (or to other state-
     approved landfills). The remainder of the City’s solid waste requiring disposal is
     sent to the Covanta Energy waste-to-energy cogeneration facility at the Fink Road
     Landfill.
    Energy & Telecommunications – Oakdale residents and businesses have a
     choice of electric and telecommunications providers. Electric service is provided
     to the City by both the Modesto Irrigation District (MID) and Pacific Gas and
     Electric (PG&E). Natural gas service is provided by PG&E. Several companies
     offer telephone, television, internet and other telecommunication services within
     the City.
The General Plan includes polices to ensure that the City and new development plan
and allocate resources for efficient and dependable infrastructure systems. In
addition, water conservation, recycled water use, stormwater pollution control,
recycling, energy conservation, local production of renewable energy, and other
efforts are identified to promote environmental sustainability.

                                             City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
  Policy Framework
PF-1: WATER
Goal PF-1
A sustainable supply of water delivered through an efficient
infrastructure system to meet existing and future needs.
 WATER SERVICE POLICIES
PF-1.1    Reliable Supply and Distribution. Maintain a reliable supply of high quality
          water and a cost-effective distribution system to meet normal and
          emergency demands in both wet and dry years. (MP, EV-IP1)
PF-1.2    Urban Water Management Plan. Regularly review and update the City’s
          Urban Water Management Plan and other water master planning and
          capital improvement tools to ensure adequate water supply, infrastructure,
          maintenance, rehabilitation, funding and conservation measures. (MP, PF-
          IP1)
PF 1.3    New Development. Require new development to demonstrate the
          availability of adequate water supply (either existing water supply or
          provision of new water sources) and infrastructure in accordance with city
          plans and standards. Ensure that new development constructs, dedicates
          and/or pays its fair share contribution to the water supply, treatment,
          storage, and distribution system necessary to serve the demands created by
          the development. (RDR, MP, OFB)
PF 1.4    Existing OID Facilities. Coordinate with OID on the potential abandonment,
          relocation and/or reuse of existing facilities and easements within the City
          where appropriate. (RDR, JP)
PF-1.5    Water Well Use. Discourage the use of private wells for domestic water use
          when connection to the City’s water system is feasible. (RDR)
PF-1.6    Groundwater. Monitor and protect the quality and quantity of groundwater.
          (OFB, IGC, PF-IP2)
PF-1.7    Groundwater Recharge. Preserve areas that provide important                      Also See Natural Resources

PF-2.7  Localized Wastewater Treatment. Explore allowing localized wastewater
        treatment systems in the City, where appropriate. (RDR)
PF-2.8  Septic Systems. Eliminate the use of septic systems when connection to the
        City’s wastewater system is feasible. (RDR, OFB)
PF-2.9  Monitoring Discharge. Continue to monitor uses that may generate toxic or
        potentially hazardous substances to prevent contamination of water and
        wastewater. (MP, OFB)

PF-3: STORM DRAINAGE
Goal PF-3
A comprehensive storm drainage system that protects public safety
and water quality.
 STORM DRAINAGE POLICIES
PF-3.1  Adequate Infrastructure. Ensure that the City’s storm drainage system is         Also See Public Health & Safety
        adequately sized, maintained and upgraded to accommodate stormwater                                      Element
        runoff and prevent flooding. (MP, EV-IP1)
PF-3.2  Storm Drainage Planning. Regularly review and update the City’s Storm
        Drainage Study and other storm drainage master planning and capital
                                                 PUBLIC FACILITIES                  PF-7

                             City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                       improvement tools to ensure adequate capacity, infrastructure, treatment,
                                       maintenance, rehabilitation, and funding. (MP, PF-IP1)
                             PF-3.3    New Development. Require new development to prepare drainage studies
                                       to demonstrate no net increase in stormwater runoff in compliance with City
                                       plans and standards. Ensure that new development constructs, dedicates
                                       and/or pays its fair share contribution to the storm drainage system
                                       necessary to serve the demands created by the development. (RDR, MP,
                                       OFB)
                             PF-3.4    Maintenance of Facilities. Require new development to create mechanisms
                                       to fund ongoing maintenance of stormwater drainage, basin and treatment
                                       facilities. (RDR, OFB)
                             PF-3.5    Deficient Areas. Prioritize the construction of storm drainage infrastructure
                                       improvements in areas where deficient service exists (such as older parts of
                                       the City prone to street flooding) to minimize flooding. (MP, IGC)
                             PF-3.6    Discharge to OID Infrastructure. Consider alternate drainage solutions in
                                       areas where stormwater is currently discharged into Oakdale Irrigation
                                       District infrastructure. (MP, IGC)
                             PF-3.7    Siting of Facilities. Site detention basins and drainage channels in locations
                                       that adequately retain, detain, and convey stormwater. (RDR, MP)
Also See Community Services PF-3.8     Facility Design. Design stormwater detention basins and drainage systems
                    Element            to be environmentally sustainable, appear natural in character, and to be
                                       compatible with surrounding uses. Allow drainage facilities to be located
                                       within parks when they provide for dual use with dry weather recreation,
                                       such as sports fields within detention basins. (RDR, MP)
                              STORMWATER QUALITY POLICIES
                             PF-3.9    Stormwater Management Program. Regularly review and update the City’s
                                       Storm Water Management Program and Storm Water Management
                                       Discharge Ordinance to ensure adequate and up-to-date stormwater
                                       pollution control measures. (MP)
 Also See Natural Resources PF-3.10    Stormwater Quality. Require new development and redevelopment to
                    Element            minimize stormwater runoff and pollutants entering drainage facilities by
                                       incorporating Low Impact Development (LID) measures and appropriate Best
                                       Management Practices (BMPs) consistent with the City’s NPDES permit and
                                       Regional Water Quality Control Board regulations. (RDR)
                         PF-8                  PUBLIC FACILITIES

                                                   City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
          STORMWATER QUALITY
          Low Impact Development
          Low Impact Development (LID) emphasizes the use of small-scale, natural, constructed,
          and proprietary drainage features to capture urban runoff and precipitation. LID
          practices promote the use of natural systems for infiltration, evapotranspiration, and
          reuse of rainwater. These practices can effectively remove nutrients, pathogens, and
          metals from stormwater, and reduce the volume and intensity of stormwater flows.
          Typical LID elements include:
                Disconnected roof drains
                Disconnected and separated pavement (e.g., detached sidewalks)
                Bioretention facilities, rain gardens, and bioswales
                Tree planting
                Grass swales and channels
                Curb cuts and vegetated filter strips
                Impervious surface reduction – permeable/porous pavements
                Stream buffers
                Soil amendments
                Pollution prevention and good housekeeping practices
PF-4: SOLID WASTE
Goal PF-4
Reduction in the generation and disposal of solid waste.
 SOLID WASTE POLICIES
PF-4.1  Adequate Services. Support efforts to maintain adequate solid waste
        facilities and services by working with the local solid waste collection,
        disposal, and recycling service provider. (JP)
PF-4.2  New Development. Require that new development is approved contingent
        upon its ability to be served with sufficient solid waste processing, recycling,
        transportation, and disposal. (RDR, JP)
PF-4.3  AB 939. Continue to participate in the Stanislaus County Regional Solid                     Also See City of Oakdale Climate
        Waste Planning Agency to further partner, plan for and document                               Action Plan for additional GHG
        compliance with AB 939 source reduction, diversion and recycling                                reduction measures related to
        requirements. (IGC, NR-IP5)                                                                        solid waste diversion rates.
PF-4.4  Residential Recycling. Work with the local solid waste service provider to
        implement a residential recycling program for multi-family residential uses
        and to improve the existing recycling program for single-family residential
        uses to increase the diversion of solid waste from landfills consistent with AB
        939 and the Oakdale Climate Action Plan. (JP, PI, NR-IP5)
                                                         PUBLIC FACILITIES                       PF-9

                                  City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                  PF-4.5    Additional Recycling Programs. Work with the local solid waste service
                                            provider to establish and improve commercial, industrial, and construction
                                            recycling programs to increase the diversion of solid waste stream from
                                            landfills consistent with AB 939 and the Oakdale Climate Action Plan. (JP,
                                            PI, NR-IP5)
                                  PF-4.6    Recycled Materials Use. Encourage the use of recycled materials in new
                                            construction. (JP, PI, NR-IP5)
                                  PF-4.7    Hazardous Wastes. Support the local solid waste service provider’s
                                            hazardous waste collection programs, including community-wide events that
                                            provide for disposal of household hazardous waste, electronic equipment,
                                            and large items. (JP, PI)
                                  PF-4.8    Community Clean-Up Events. Sponsor annual community clean-up events,
                                            in which volunteers and community organizers help pick up litter along the
                                            Stanislaus River, roadways, parks and other public areas. (JP, PI)
                                  PF-4.9    Education and Communication. Sponsor educational programs on the
                                            benefits of solid waste diversion and recycling, and communicate recycling
                                            options and locations in Oakdale to the public. (JP, PI)

PF-5.4  Energy Conserving Land Use Practices. Implement energy conserving land             Also See Land Use & Community
        use practices including compact development, provision of bikeways and                  Form and Mobility Elements
        pedestrian paths, and the incorporation of transit routes and facilities. (RDR,
        MP, NR-IP5)
PF-5.5  Heat Gain Reduction. Encourage site and building designs that reduce
        exterior heat gain and heat island effects (e.g., tree planting, reflective
        paving materials, covered parking, cool roofs). (RDR, NR-IP5)
PF-5.6  Building Orientations. Require, to the extent feasible, building orientations
        and landscaping designs that promote the use of natural lighting, take
        advantage of passive summer cooling and winter solar access, and
        incorporate other techniques to reduce energy demands. (RDR, NR-IP5)
PF-5.7  Renewable Energy. Require new industrial users, and encourage all other
        new development when financially feasible, to install renewable energy
        systems and facilities (e.g., solar) consistent with the Oakdale Climate Action
        Plan.(RDR, NR-IP5)
PF-5.8  Energy Efficiency. Encourage all new development to implement additional
        energy efficient measures beyond what is required by State law to exceed
        minimum energy efficiency requirements consistent with the Oakdale
        Climate Action Plan. (RDR, NR-IP5)
PF-5.9  New Residential Development. Require new residential development to
        incorporate prewiring for solar or other renewable energy systems, and
        offer optional features that would allow for increased energy efficiency in
        homes (e.g., electric vehicle plugs, zoned heating and cooling, automated
        lighting and heating/cooling systems). (RDR, NR-IP5)
PF-5.10 City Facilities. Install energy-efficient lighting, appliances, and alternative-
        energy infrastructure (e.g., solar panels) in City facilities, where
        economically feasible. (OFB, NR-IP5)
PF-5.11 Retrofit Existing Buildings. Coordinate with local energy providers to
        increase energy efficiency by promoting the retrofit and renovation of
        existing buildings through energy rebates and incentives consistent with the
        Oakdale Climate Action Plan. (RDR, MP, JP, NR-IP5)
PF-5.12 Undergrounding Utilities. Work with local energy providers to underground
        existing energy facilities and ensure that new facilities are constructed below
        ground. (RDR, JP)
PF-5.13 Education. Coordinate with local energy providers to increase awareness of
        energy conservation through public education programs. (JP, PI)

     PF-6: TELECOMMUNICATIONS
     Goal PF-6
     Quality communication systems that enhance economic development,
     governmental efficiency, and equitable access for all.
      TELECOMMUNICATIONS POLICIES
     PF-6.1    Access. Coordinate with local internet, television, telephone, cellular and
               other telecommunications service providers to ensure access to and
               availability of a wide range of state-of-the-art telecommunication systems
               and services throughout the City. (JP)
     PF-6.2    Service for All. Work with local telecommunications service providers to
               retrofit areas that are not currently served by telecommunication
               technologies and promote strategic long-range planning of facilities for
               newly developing areas. (RDR, JP)
     PF-6.3    New Development. Establish requirements for the installation of state-of-the-
               art telecommunications technologies in new planned communities, office,
               commercial and industrial developments. (RDR, JP)
     PF-6.4    Residential Access. Encourage the installation of telecommunications
               improvements (e.g., internet) in every city household to facilitate resident
               access to information. (RDR, JP)
     PF-6.5    Co-location. Require compatible co-location of telecommunication facilities
               that are designed in a manner to minimize visual impacts on surrounding
               uses and to be as unobtrusive as possible. (RDR, JP)
     PF-6.6    Undergrounding Utilities. Work with local telecommunications service
               providers to underground existing telecommunications facilities and ensure
               that new facilities are constructed below ground. (RDR, JP)
     PF-6.7    City Operations. Expand the use of telecommunications and new
               technologies to enhance the performance of internal City operations and the
               delivery of public services. (OFB, JP)
PF-12                 PUBLIC FACILITIES
OAKDALE 2030 GENERAL PLAN
COMMUNITY SERVICES

                                             City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
         Community Services
The Community Services Element establishes requirements for the delivery of police
and fire protection, parks and recreation, educational facilities, libraries and health
care within the City of Oakdale. The intent is to provide quality public services
equitably to all residents and businesses within the City, as well as ensure a safe
place to live and do business.
    Our community services vision includes…
        Cost effective and sustainable services
                                                                                        CONTENTS
        Reliable law enforcement, fire protection and emergency medical                Context
         response
                                                                                        Policy Framework
        Accessible parks and recreation facilities promoting healthy lifestyles
                                                                                        CS-1    Police Protection
        Improved integration and community use of the Stanislaus River
         corridor                                                                       CS-2    Fire Protection
        Quality school, library, hospital and medical services                         CS-3    Parks and Recreation
                                                                                        CS-4    Educational Facilities
                                                                                        CS-5    Libraries
                                                                                        CS-6    Health Care
                                            COMMUNITY SERVICES                         CS-1

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
      Context
    Community services play a critical role in health, livability and economic growth.
    The City of Oakdale seeks to provide a broad range of quality facilities and services
    to meet diverse community needs. Facilities and services are to be located and
    programmed to provide efficient, equitable and consistent levels of service.
    Community services in Oakdale are supplied by a combination of City and outside
    providers, with key facilities illustrated on Figure CS-1:
       Police Protection - The Oakdale Police Department provides law enforcement
        services within the City, and the Stanislaus County Sheriff’s Department
        provides law enforcement services outside the City. The Oakdale Police
        Department has one centrally located station, and is organized within three
        different divisions: Administrative Services, Field Services, and Special Services.
        The Police Department works closely with the Office of Emergency Services, and
        it is normal practice for the Department to provide law enforcement assistance
        in nearby areas. Future growth will necessitate additional staffing, facility,
        equipment and associated funding needs.
       Fire Protection - The City of Oakdale Fire Department, augmented by Oakdale
        Rural Fire Protection District staff, is the first responder on fire and medical
        emergencies within the City limits and for areas outside of the City limits.
        The City Fire Department has reciprocal Mutual Aid and Automatic Aid
        agreements with the Oakdale Rural Fire Protection District and the
        Stanislaus Consolidated Fire Protection District, which enhance level of

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
        service. The City is served by two fire stations, and has a Class 4 Insurance
        Service Office (ISO) rating. Oakdale Rural Fire Protection District also has
        one fire station in the City. Future growth will require additional resources to
        meet established response time standards. In addition, coordination between
        the City and Oakdale Rural Fire Protection District will continue as the City’s
        boundaries expand.
       Parks & Recreation - The City of Oakdale Parks and Recreation Department
        is responsible for providing and maintaining all City parks, recreation
        facilities and programs. The City’s park system includes community,
        neighborhood, mini and linear parks, as well as a community center and
        plaza, senior center, and multi-use buildings. Immediately outside the City
        limits along the Stanislaus River are the Oakdale Recreation Area, Valley
        Oak Recreation Area, and Stanley Wakefield Wilderness Area. Future
        growth will necessitate additional land, staffing, facility, program,
        maintenance and related funding needs.
       Educational Facilities - The Oakdale Joint Unified School District (OJUSD)
        serves Oakdale residents and portions of the surrounding area. The OJUSD
        provides elementary schools, a junior high school, a comprehensive high
        school, and alternative high school and adult education facilities. Student
        generation and school capacity will need to continue to be closely
        monitored as the City grows. Yosemite Community College District (YCCD)
        encompasses the City of Oakdale and surrounding area. The YCCD offers
        general education courses through the Oakdale Outreach site at Oakdale
        High School, and has approached the City with possible plans to build a
        satellite educational center in Oakdale.
       Libraries - The Stanislaus County Library system provides library services
        throughout the County, including a centrally located branch in the City of
        Oakdale. The libraries in Stanislaus County are funded in large part by a
        1/8-cent dedicated sales tax first passed by the voters in 1995, again in
        1999 and in 2004. The current tax is in effect until June 30, 2013.
       Health Care – Oak Valley Hospital, a full service nonprofit public hospital,
        is located within the City of Oakdale. Oak Valley recently completed a new
        replacement hospital facility within the City.
    The General Plan includes polices that advocate adequate police and fire services
    and facilities to protect the long-term health, safety and well-being of the
    community; accessible parks, schools and libraries that promote life-long activity
    and learning, serving as focal points of community interaction and identify; and
    high quality health care facilities for the City’s residents.
CS-4                 COMMUNITY SERVICES

                                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
  Policy Framework
CS-1: POLICE PROTECTION
Goal CS-1
A safe and secure community with responsive law enforcement
services.
 POLICE PROTECTION POLICIES
CS-1.1    Police Master Plan. Prepare and maintain a Police Master Plan to address
          needs, goals and priorities for staffing, facilities, services, and funding. (CS-
          IP1, CS-IP2)
CS-1.2    Service Goal. Maintain an initial response time for:
              Priority 1 calls of no more than 6 minutes;
              Priority 2 calls of no more than 7 minutes; and
              Priority 3 calls of no more than 17 minutes. (OFB, CS-IP2)
CS-1.3    Adequate Personnel and Equipment. Maintain adequate levels of sworn
          officers, support staff, volunteers, equipment, technology, and training to
          provide effective and highly visible police protection services within the City.
          (OFB, CS-IP2)
CS-1.4    Special Funds. Adopt and renew special funds, such as the City’s Public               Also See Economic Vitality
          Safety CFD, to assist in funding police operations and facilities that enable                          Element
          the City to maintain adequate levels of police protection. (OFB, EV-IP1)
CS-1.5    Development Fees. Continue to collect the City’s Police Capital Facilities Fee
          from new development to fund the construction or purchase of police
          facilities required to service new growth areas. (RDR, OFB)
CS-1.6    Review of Development Proposals. Include the Police Department in the
          review of development proposals to ensure that projects adequately address
          crime and safety. (RDR)
CS-1.7    Security and Design Features. Promote the implementation of Crime
          Prevention Through Environmental Design (CPTED) principles in new
          development projects and public improvements to minimize opportunities for
          criminal activity. (RDR)
CS-1.8    Mutual Aid. Coordinate with appropriate law enforcement agencies to
          promote regional cooperation and provide mutual aid during emergency
          situations. (IGC)

                                    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                    CS-1.9    Education. Support community-based service and education programs
                                              designed to prevent crime, such as the Neighborhood Watch Program. (PI)
                                    CS-2: FIRE PROTECTION
                                    Goal CS-2
                                    Protection of life and property through adequate fire protection and
                                    emergency medical services.
                                     FIRE PROTECTION POLICIES
                                    CS-2.1    Fire Master Plan. Regularly review and maintain the City’s Fire Master Plan
                                              to address needs, goals and priorities for staffing, facilities, services and
                                              funding. (MP, CS-IP1)
                                    CS-2.2    Service Goal. Maintain an initial response time of:
                                                  7 minutes, 90 percent of the time to treat medical patients and control
                                                   small fires; and
                                                  11 minutes, 90 percent of the time for a multiple-unit response for
                                                   serious emergencies. (MP, OFB)
                                    CS-2.3    Adequate Personnel and Equipment. Maintain adequate staffing,
                                              equipment, technology and training to provide effective and efficient fire
                                              protection and emergency medical services within the City. (MP, OFB)
                                    CS-2.4    Enforcement of Codes. Continue to enforce all relevant codes and
                                              ordinances for existing buildings and new construction to reduce the risk of
                                              fire hazards. Encourage installation of private early warning and fire
                                              suppression systems. (RDR, OFB)
Also See Public Facilities Element CS-2.5     Adequate Water Supply. Maintain adequate water supply and fire flow
                                              pressure as specified in the Fire Master Plan in both existing and new
                                              development areas. (RDR, MP)
      Also See Economic Vitality CS-2.6       Special Funds. Adopt and renew special funds, such as the City’s Public
                           Element            Safety CFD, to assist in funding fire operations and facilities that enable the
                                              City to maintain adequate levels of fire protection. (OFB, EV-IP1)
                                    CS-2.7    Development Fees. Continue to collect the City’s Fire Capital Facilities Fee
                                              from new development to fund the construction of fire protection facilities
                                              required to service new growth areas. (RDR, OFB)
                                    CS-2.8    Review of Development Proposals. Include the Fire Department in the
                                              review of development proposals to ensure that projects adequately address
                                              safe design and on-site fire protection. (RDR)
                                CS-6                COMMUNITY SERVICES

                                           City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
CS-2.9  Fire Access Routes. Include at least two fire access routes for all larger new
        development projects, as determined by the Oakdale Fire Department.
        (RDR)
CS-2.10 Fire Stations. Ensure that fire stations are located, and their construction
        phased, to provide appropriate service levels to surrounding areas. (RDR,
        MP, OFB)
CS-2.11 Service Areas. Adjust the service area boundaries of the Oakdale Fire
        Department and the Oakdale Rural Fire District through a joint powers
        agreement or other mechanisms to provide adequate emergency response
        as the City limits expand. (MP, IGC)
CS-2.12 Mutual Aid. Coordinate with appropriate fire protection agencies to
        promote regional cooperation and provide mutual aid during emergency
        situations. (MP, IGC)
CS-2.13 Education. Support local, state and federal programs designed to inform
        and educate the public concerning fire prevention and suppression. (PI)
 WILDLAND FIRE HAZARDS POLICIES
CS-2.14 Weed Abatement. Enforce the City’s weed/hazard abatement program
        and other relevant codes and ordinances designed to abate fire hazards on
        private residential and non-residential uses and on City-owned properties.
        (OFB)
CS-2.15 Urban/Wildland Interface: Design and construct new development
        proposed within or adjacent to fire hazards zones, such as the Stanislaus
        River Corridor, to reduce exposure to fire hazards and facilitate fire
        suppression efforts in the event of a wildfire. (RDR)
CS-2.16 Wildland Fire Education. Educate the public about wildland fire prevention
        techniques such as site design, landscaping, and defensible space
        vegetation management practices to minimize potential wildland fire
        hazards. (PI)

                                CS-3: PARKS AND RECREATION
                                Goal CS-3
                                An integrated system of parks, open space, and recreational facilities
                                that are programmed to benefit all members of the community.
                                 PARKS AND RECREATION POLICIES
                                CS-3.1    Open Space, Recreation, and Conservation Master Plan. Regularly review
                                          and maintain the City’s Open Space, Recreation, and Conservation Master
                                          Plan (OSRCMP) to address park and recreation standards, sites, facilities,
                                          programs and funding. (MP)
                                CS-3.2    Park Land Standard. Provide a minimum of five (5) acres of parkland per
                                          1,000 residents through a combination of active and passive lands. (RDR,
                                          MP)
Also See Land Use & Community CS-3.3      Park Types and Siting. Develop a diverse and accessible system of park
                  Form Element            and recreation facilities throughout Oakdale in accordance with the
                                          definitions and guidelines specified on Table CS-1 and the OSRCMP. (MP,
                                          OFB)
                                CS-3.4    New Development Dedication and Funding. Require new residential
                                          development to dedicate land and provide adequate funding through a
                                          variety of mechanisms such as the City’s Capital Facilities Fee and
                                          Community Facilities Districts for the initial construction and ongoing
                                          maintenance/operation of public parks and recreation facilities, open
                                          space, and landscape areas in accordance with the City’s parkland
                                          standards. (RDR, OFB)
                                CS-3.5    Non-traditional Parklands. Consider allocating partial park credits for non-
                                          traditional parklands that provide active and passive recreational value.
                                          (RDR, MP)
                                CS-3.6    Phasing. Require that parks and recreational facilities be phased to be
                                          available as adjacent residential uses are developed. (RDR)
                                CS-3.7    Flexibility in Standards. Retain flexibility in applying parks standards, in
                                          terms of size, facilities and service areas, to adjust to existing and future
                                          needs. (RDR, MP)
                                CS-3.8    Incentives. Consider incentives, such as density bonuses, for development
                                          proposals which offer parkland dedications beyond those required, and/or
                                          encourage the provision of privately-maintained open space in planned
                                          developments. (RDR)

     City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
     CS-3.12   Park Landscaping. Require the use of native, drought-tolerant plants that
               are non-allergenic, when feasible, consistent with the City’s existing
               ordinances. (RDR, MP)
     CS-3.13   River Corridor. Establish an open space/scenic corridor along the
               Stanislaus River. Enhance public access and use of the corridor through
               development and implementation of the Stanislaus River Corridor Access
               Plan. (CS-IP3)
                STANISLAUS RIVER CORRIDOR ACCESS PLAN
                The Stanislaus River Corridor Access Plan is intended to provide a system of preserved
                lands and habitat, with connecting trails and access points, along the Stanislaus River
                Corridor through the City of Oakdale. The Plan will include a coordinated multi-agency
                management strategy to respect natural waterways and protect natural resources,
                encourage compatible recreational opportunities that do not damage sensitive areas,
                and provide for a continuous and coordinated system of connecting corridor trails. This
                effort could be managed by a committee to be established as part of the plan
                preparation process. Key objectives include:
                      Coordinate the multiple agencies with jurisdiction in the River Corridor through a
                       single planning and management strategy
                      Implement a continuous trail system through the River Corridor
                      Provide trail connections and staging areas from Oakdale to the River Corridor
                      Connect with the adjacent Oakdale Recreation Area, Valley Oak Recreation
                       Area, and Stanley Wakefield Wilderness Area
                      Coordinate with potential regional river corridor planning and trail system efforts
                      Explore opportunities to incorporate low-intensity recreational facilities
                      Preserve the natural habitat, scenic quality, and heritage of the River Corridor
                      Identify opportunities for environmental interpretation and education
                      Explore possibilities to attract visitors and related businesses
                      Identify and secure potential funding sources for project implementation
                  The preparation of the Stanislaus River Corridor Access Plan is contingent upon the
                  availability of funding.
     CS-3.14   Kerr Park. Maintain the Kerr Park floodplain in its natural state and link it
               with the Stanislaus River Corridor and nearby Stanley Wakefield
               Wilderness Area. (MP)
     CS-3.15   Youth, Adults, and Seniors. Support a wide variety of recreational
               programming for citizens of all ages and abilities, including youths, adults,
               and seniors. (MP, OFB)
     CS-3.16   Volunteer Programs. Encourage opportunities for citizens to participate in
               enhancing City recreational programs including the Adopt-A-Park, Adopt-
               A-Trail, and Team-Up Against Graffiti Programs. (OFB, PI)
     CS-3.17   Regional Coordination. Coordinate with other jurisdictions and agencies to
               provide regional recreation facilities, where appropriate. (IGC)

Goal CS-4
Superior educational opportunities and facilities for all members of the
community.
 EDUCATIONAL FACILITIES POLICIES
CS-4.1   Educational Services. Support public school districts, private schools, and
         higher education institutions in providing educational services. (JP)
CS-4.2   School Capacity. Cooperate with school districts, within the limits of State
         law, to ensure that school facilities with sufficient capacity are reserved,
         constructed and phased to meet the needs of current and projected
         enrollment. (RDR, JP)
CS-4.3   School Siting. Coordinate with school districts to ensure that schools are         Also See Land Use & Community
         efficiently and equitably sited throughout the City. Schools should be located                       Form Element
         to provide for safe and convenient access by students, and be centrally
         positioned within neighborhoods as focal points when feasible. (RDR, JP)
CS-4.4   Joint Use. Coordinate with school districts, private schools, and higher
         education institutions to pursue the joint use of school, park, and other
         facilities especially when school is not in session (i.e., weekends and summer
         vacation). Joint use agreements should be executed to maximize public use
         of facilities, minimize duplication of services, and facilitate shared financial
         and operational responsibilities. (JP)
CS-4.5   Review of Development Proposals. Provide school districts an opportunity
         to review and comment on residential development proposals to ensure that
         projects adequately address school capacity issues. (RDR, JP)
CS-4.6   Funding Sources. Cooperate with school districts in identifying and pursuing
         sources of funding for the rehabilitation, improvement, and expansion of
         existing schools and construction of future school facilities. (JP)
CS-4.7   New School Facilities. Ensure that new residential development, to the
         extent permissible under State law, fully mitigates its impact on school

               facilities through the payment of fees or other negotiated methods. Funding
               agreements between the project proponent and school district, when
               required, shall be entered into prior to the issuance of building permits.

OAKDALE 2030 GENERAL PLAN
NATURAL RESOURCES

                                             City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                 Natural Resources
The Natural Resources Element guides the conservation of Oakdale’s natural
and cultural resources, and the long-term preservation of open space lands. The
intent is to support the protection and wise use of significant resources, minimize
the impacts of growth on those resources, and ensure their sustainability and
                                                                                    CONTENTS
availability for future generations.
                                                                                    Context
    Our natural resources vision includes…
                                                                                    Policy Framework
     Preserved habitat, open space and natural resources
                                                                                    NR-1    Open Space and Biological
         An enhanced Stanislaus River Corridor                                             Resources
         Continued production on adjacent agricultural lands                       NR-2    Agricultural Resources
         Reduced air quality and greenhouse gas emissions                          NR-3    Air Quality and Climate
         Respect for the city’s heritage and cultural resources                            Change
                                                                                    NR-4    Water Resources and
                                                                                            Quality
                                                                                    NR-5    Mineral Resources
                                                                                    NR-6    Visual Resources
                                                                                    NR-7    Cultural Resources
                                              NATURAL RESOURCES                    NR-1

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
       Context
    The City of Oakdale values its natural and cultural resources and promotes
    environmental sustainability as a core principle. The community is committed to
    protecting and enhancing its unique habitats, nearby agricultural lands, air and
    water quality, mineral and visual resources, and its historic and cultural roots. A
    healthy natural environment contributes directly to existing and future quality of
    life. Key resources addressed by this element include:
         Open Space and Biological Resources – Natural habitats within the City
          and surrounding area include perennial grasslands, riparian woodlands,
          oak woodlands, and a variety of wetlands including vernal pools, seasonal
          wetlands, freshwater marshes, ponds, streams, and rivers (see Figure NR-1).
          Though much of these habitats have been lost or altered due to agriculture
          or urban development, the presence of scattered portions of undeveloped
          habitat and proximity to the Stanislaus River and its tributaries does provide
          suitable habitat for a variety of common and special-status plant and animal
          species.
         Agricultural Resources – Farming is important to the economy of both
          Oakdale and Stanislaus County. There are pockets of active agricultural
          lands within the city limits targeted primarily for future urban use. A majority
          of the lands outside the City, and north of the Stanislaus River within the
          City’s Sphere of Influence, are designated for long-term agricultural
          production. Principal agricultural products within the area include milk,
          almonds, chicken, cattle, and walnuts. Farmlands in the Planning Area,
          as classified by the California Department of Conservation Farmland

                                                        Air Quality and Climate Change – The City of Oakdale and
                                                         surrounding region are located within the San Joaquin Valley Air
                                                         Basin (SJVAB) and within the jurisdiction of the San Joaquin Valley Air
                                                         Pollution Control District. Ozone and particulate matter pollution levels
                                                         in the San Joaquin Valley are among the worst in the nation, and the
                                                         basin is designated a nonattainment area for several state- and
                                                         federal-level criteria air quality pollutants. The City of Oakdale, like the
                                                         rest of the cities in California, is also likely to face challenges in the
                                                         21st Century related to climate change. California’s Global Warming
                                                         Solutions Act of 2006 (AB 32), directs the state to reduce state-wide
                                                         GHG emissions to 1990 levels by 2020. Concurrent with adoption of
                                                         the 2030 General Plan, the City adopted a Climate Action Plan to
                                                         ensure that Oakdale does its part to meet the mandates of AB 32.
                                                         Additionally, the City has taken proactive steps to address climate
                                                         change, such as replacing features at water well sites and lift stations
                                                         that will make it more energy efficient.

City of Oakdale                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   AGRICULTURAL RESOURCES

  This Page is Intentionally Left Blank
 

                                     City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
 Water Resources and Quality - The Stanislaus River is the only major
  surface water body in the City. From its headwaters in the Sierra, the
  river flows in a west-southwesterly direction, emptying into the San
  Joaquin River and ultimately the San Francisco Bay. Two major dams
  are located along the Stanislaus River upstream of the City, the
  Tulloch and the New Melones Reservoirs. Water quality in the
  Stanislaus River is relatively good. There are also a number of
  local/minor surface water bodies in the City and adjacent areas (See
  Figure NR-3). Oakdale primarily overlies the Modesto Groundwater
  Subbasin. Groundwater levels within this basin have fluctuated over
  the last 40 years within approximately 20 feet of 1970 levels, with
  some portions of the basin showing a general decline over the last 20
  years. Groundwater quality is generally good, with some localized
  areas of hard water and high chloride, boron, Dibromochloropropane
  (DBCP), nitrate, iron, and manganese. Areas that contribute to
  groundwater recharge are also shown on Figure NR-3.
 Mineral Resources – The California Geological Survey has defined
  areas along the Stanislaus River within the City and surrounding area
  as Mineral Resource Zone 2 (MRZ-2). This designation indicates a high
  likelihood for occurrence of significant mineral deposits. While there
  are no active mining operations in the City or immediately surrounding
  area, historical mineral production included construction aggregate
  along the Stanislaus River. In addition, three plugged and abandoned
  oil wells are located outside of the City limits.  
 Visual Resources –  Key visual resources within Oakdale consist of
  buildings within the City’s historic Downtown, its nearby historic
  neighborhoods, and views of the Stanislaus River corridor. Other
  important visual resources include views to the extensive agricultural
  and rural lands surrounding the City, as well as distant views to the
  east of the Sierra Nevada mountain range. Development within the
  City does produce light and glare that can impact views of the night
  sky.
 Cultural Resources – The City and surrounding area contain various
  paleontological, archaeological, and historic resources. Included are
  a number of identified historic and prehistoric archaeological sites.
  Built environment resources in Oakdale include some of the first homes
  constructed in the City dating from the 1870s and 1880s, early-
  twentieth-century homes, early brick buildings in the Downtown dating
  from the 1910s to 1920s, and buildings and structures associated with
  the railroad and the processing of agricultural goods.
  A number of these structures have previously been identified as
  potentially eligible for the National Register of Historic Places (NHRP).
  The First National Bank Building, built in 1909 and located at the
  northwest Corner of F Street and Yosemite Avenue, is the only NRHP
  listed building in the City.
