                                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
         The General Plan includes policies that protect the ecological needs
         of threatened, endangered or otherwise sensitive species and their
         habitats; support the long-term presence and viability of agriculture;
         reduce emissions of criteria air quality pollutants and greenhouse
         gasses; conserve ground and surface water quality and resources;
         manage mineral deposits; enhance scenic corridors and viewsheds;
         and ensure important paleontological, archaeological, and historic
         resources are protected and preserved as appropriate.
  Policy Framework
NR-1: OPEN SPACE AND BIOLOGICAL
            RESOURCES
Goal NR-1
Conservation and enhancement of Oakdale’s open spaces and
significant biological resources.
 OPEN SPACE AND BIOLOGICAL RESOURCE POLICIES
NR-1.1    Open Space. Ensure the conservation of lands designated for open space
          within the City. (RDR, MP, NR-IP1)
NR-1.2    Coordinated Protection. Work with Stanislaus County and surrounding
          jurisdictions to protect and acquire open space lands within and adjacent
          to Oakdale’s Planning Area. (MP, IGC)
NR-1.3    Stanislaus River Corridor. Coordinate with the applicable resource                Also See Community Services
          agencies to develop and implement the Stanislaus River Corridor Access                               Element
          Plan to preserve natural open space and biological resources, while
          providing access to and recreational opportunities along the river. (CS-IP3)
NR-1.4    Preservation. Preserve unique and valuable natural resources and
          associated habitats, including special-status species, in coordination with
          federal, state, and local resource agencies. (RDR, IGC)
NR-1.5    Resources Assessment. Require discretionary development proposals that
          could potentially impact natural resources to conduct a biological resources
          assessment to ensure that project-related impacts are considered and
          mitigated consistent with local, state and federal regulations. (RDR)
NR-1.6    Avoidance. Ensure new development projects avoid, to the extent feasible,
          significant biological resources (e.g. areas of rare, threatened, or
          endangered species). (RDR)
                                               NATURAL RESOURCES                       NR-9

                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                               NR-1.7    Buffers. Require the provision and maintenance of buffers between
                                         sensitive biological resources and adjacent urban uses to minimize
                                         disturbance of the resources, as appropriate. (RDR)
                               NR-1.8    Tree Preservation. Preserve significant native and heritage trees as defined
                                         by the City of Oakdale Zoning Code (Section 36-28), and reduce the loss
                                         of these trees through mitigation and replanting programs, when feasible.
                                         (RDR)
                               NR-1.9    Wildlife Movement. Preserve, enhance, and create interconnected open
                                         space and natural areas, such as along the Stanislaus River corridor, to
                                         provide for wildlife movement and protect biodiversity. (RDR, MP, CS-IP3)
                               NR-1.10   Native Plants Use. Encourage the use of native and drought tolerant plants
                                         and trees in all public and private landscaping and revegetation projects.
                                         (RDR, MP, NR-IP5)
                               NR-1.11   Funding. Pursue available funding sources for open space acquisition,
                                         management, and enhancement. (OFB, NR-IP1, NR-IP2)
                               NR-2: AGRICULTURAL RESOURCES
                               Goal NR-2
                               Preservation of agricultural lands and operations both within and
                               outside the City’s Planning Area.
                                AGRICULTURAL RESOURCES POLICIES
                               NR-2.1    Agricultural Land Outside of City. Work with Stanislaus County and
                                         other applicable agencies to protect viable agriculture within and
Also See Land Use & Community            adjacent to Oakdale’s Planning Area. (IGC, NR-IP3)
                  Form Element NR-2.2    Agricultural Land within City. Support the continued production of existing
                                         agricultural properties within the City’s Planning Area until such properties
                                         are developed in accordance with adopted land uses. (RDR)
                               NR-2.3    Plan for Agricultural Preservation. Prepare and adopt a Plan for
                                         Agricultural Preservation consistent with the provisions of and implementing
                                         the Stanislaus County LAFCO Agricultural Preservation Policy to minimize
                                         the loss of agricultural land, in conjunction with any new Specific Plan
                                         adoption or annexation/Sphere of Influence modification. One of the
                                         strategies consistent with the LAFCO Policy may require permanent
                                         protection of similar quality farmland at a 1:1 ratio for conversion of Prime
                                         Farmland, Farmland of Statewide Importance, and Unique Farmland (as
                                         designated by the California Department of Conservation Farmland
                                         Mapping and Monitoring Program) to residential uses. (RDR, NR-IP2, NR-
                                         IP3)
Also See Land Use & Community NR-2.4     Transition to Agricultural Operations. Require new development along
                  Form Element           the planned edge of the City to provide buffer treatments, as appropriate,
                                         to protect the ongoing viability of adjacent agriculture. (RDR)
                          NR-10                 NATURAL RESOURCES

                                                 City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
NR-2.5   Right-to-Farm. Condition new residential development located adjacent
         to agricultural uses to record the City’s right-to-farm disclosure statement.
         (RDR)
NR-2.6   Farmer’s Markets. Continue to support the operation of, and provide
         venues for, farmer’s markets to allow farmers in the area to sell their
         products locally. (RDR)
NR-3: AIR QUALITY AND CLIMATE CHANGE
Goal NR-3
Improved air quality and reduced greenhouse gas emissions in the
City and region.
 AIR QUALITY AND CLIMATE CHANGE
NR-3.1   Regional Coordination. Participate in regional planning efforts including
         coordination with the San Joaquin Valley Air Pollution Control District,
         Stanislaus Council of Governments, and other jurisdictions on programs
         to reduce air quality impacts and attain state and federal air quality
         standards. (IGC, NR-IP2, NR-IP4)
NR-3.2   GHG Reduction Measures. Apply appropriate measures as defined in
         the City of Oakdale Climate Action Plan to reduce regional greenhouse
         gas emissions. (RDR, MP, OFB, LU-IP2, M-IP1, M-IP2, M-IP3, M-IP4,
         NR-IP2, NR-IP5)
           CITY OF OAKDALE CLIMATE ACTION PLAN
           Concurrent with adoption of the 2030 General Plan, the City adopted a Climate
           Action Plan (CAP). The Oakdale CAP outlines strategies, goals, and actions for
           reducing municipal and community-wide greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions to
           ensure that the City does its part to meet the mandates of California’s Global
           Warming Solutions Act of 2006 (AB 32). Strategies address energy, transportation
           and land use, solid waste and water. Key reduction measures within the CAP
           include, but are not limited to:
                Increased energy efficiency such as building energy efficiency standards and
                 rebate programs.
                Smart electric grid technology.
                Improved industrial equipment energy efficiency.
                Increased renewable energy generation including on-site renewable
                 energy systems.
                Smart growth, higher density and mixed use development.
                Reduced commuter trips through trip reduction programs, improved transit,
                 and bicycle/pedestrian planning and improvements.
                Preferred parking for energy efficient vehicles.
                Improved highway traffic flows.
                Increased solid waste diversion/recycling rates.
                Water conservation measures.
                                                  NATURAL RESOURCES                           NR-11

                          City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                          NR-3.3    Construction Emissions. Require new development projects to incorporate
                                    feasible measures that reduce emissions from construction, grading,
                                    excavation, and demolition activities to avoid, minimize, and/or offset
                                    their impacts consistent with San Joaquin Valley Air Pollution Control
                                    District requirements. (RDR, IGC)
                          NR-3.4    Operational Emissions. Require new development projects to incorporate
                                    feasible measures that reduce operational emissions through project and
                                    site design and use of best management practices to avoid, minimize,
                                    and/or offset their impacts consistent with San Joaquin Valley Air
                                    Pollution Control District requirements. (RDR, IGC)
                          NR-3.5    SJVAPCD Consultation. Require consultation and coordination with the
                                    San Joaquin Valley Air Pollution Control District for any projects that may
                                    have a potential health risk impact or may expose the public to
                                    hazardous air pollutants, and on compliance with adopted rules and
                                    regulations. (RDR, IGC)
                          NR-3.6    Toxic Air Pollutants. Locate uses, facilities and operations that may
                                    produce toxic or hazardous air pollutants (e.g., industrial uses, highways)
                                    an adequate distance from sensitive receptors (e.g., housing and
                                    schools), consistent with California Air Resources Board
                                    recommendations. (RDR, IGC)
                          NR-3.7    Odors. Require that adequate buffer distances be provided between odor
                                    sources and sensitive receptors. (RDR)
                          NR-3.8    Truck Delivery Schedules. Encourage businesses to alter local truck
                                    delivery schedules to occur during non-peak hours, when feasible.
                                    (RDR, PI)
Also See Mobility Element NR-3.9    Large Employers. Encourage large employers to allow flexible work
                                    hours and telecommuting, and to provide incentives for employee use of
                                    alternative modes of transportation for home to work commutes including
                                    public transit and carpooling. (RDR, PI)
                          NR-3.10   City Employees. Encourage City employees through incentives and other
                                    methods to use alternative modes of transportation for home to work
                                    commutes including public transit and carpooling. Promote
                                    telecommuting, when feasible. (OFB, IGC, M-IP4, NR-IP6)
                          NR-3.11   Contractor Preference. Give preference to contractors that apply methods
                                    to minimize greenhouse gas emissions in building construction and
                                    operations, such as the use low or zero-emission vehicles and equipment.
                                    (OFB)
                          NR-3.12   City Fleet. Purchase low-emission vehicles for the City’s non-emergency
                                    fleet and use clean fuel sources for trucks and heavy equipment, when
                                    feasible. (OFB)
                     NR-12                 NATURAL RESOURCES

                                             City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
NR-3.13  Education. Participate in efforts that educate the public about air quality,
         its effects on health, and actions that can be taken to improve air quality
         and reduce greenhouse gas emissions. (PI)
NR-4: WATER RESOURCES AND QUALITY
Goal NR-4
Enhance the quality of the City’s surface water and groundwater
resources.
 WATER RESOURCE PROTECTION POLICIES
NR-4.1   Stanislaus River. Protect surface water resources in Oakdale, including
         the Stanislaus River. (RDR, MP, IGC)
NR-4.2   Groundwater Management Plan. Continue to work with applicable                  Also See Public Facilities Element
         agencies to prepare, regularly review, update, and implement
         regional groundwater management plans to ensure the sustainability
         of groundwater quality and quantity. (IGC, PF-IP3)
NR-4.3   Natural Open Space Areas. Preserve areas that provide important
         groundwater recharge, stormwater management, and water quality
         benefits such as undeveloped open spaces, natural habitat, riparian
         corridors, wetlands, and other drainage areas. (RDR, MP, NR-IP1)
 WATER QUALITY PROTECTION POLICIES
NR-4.4   National Pollution Discharge Elimination System. Regulate construction
         and operational activities to incorporate stormwater protection measures
         and best management practices in accordance with the City’s National
         Pollution Discharge Elimination System (NPDES) permit. (RDR, MP, OFB)
NR-4.5   Industrial, Agricultural, and Septic System Discharge. Regulate
         discharge from industrial users, use of agricultural chemicals (i.e.,
         pesticides) and use of septic systems in accordance with local and State
         regulations to protect the City’s natural water bodies. (RDR, IGC)
NR-4.6   Regulation of Runoff. Protect Oakdale’s water resources from
         contamination by regulating stormwater collection and conveyance to
         ensure pollutants in runoff have been reduced to the maximum extent
         practicable. (RDR, OFB)
NR-4.7   New Development. Require new development to protect the quality of             Also See Public Facilities Element
         surface and groundwater bodies and natural drainage systems through
         site design, stormwater treatment, low impact development measures,
         and best management practices. (RDR)
                                             NATURAL RESOURCES                       NR-13

                            City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                            NR-4.8    Regional Coordination. Coordinate and collaborate with agencies in the
                                      region and watershed to address water quality issues. (IGC)
                            NR-4.9    Education. Educate the public about practices and programs to minimize
                                      surface water and groundwater pollution. (PI)
                            NR-5: MINERAL RESOURCES
                            Goal NR-5
                            Protection of and access to mineral resources when compatible with
                            adjacent uses.
                             MINERAL RESOURCES POLICIES
                            NR-5.1    Significant Resources. Protect access to and availability of mineral
                                      resources identified by the State as a significant resource, and continue to
                                      regulate activities consistent with the Surface Mining and Reclamation Act
                                      and the California Environmental Quality Act. (RDR)
                            NR-5.2    Compatible Operations. Require that current and future oil, gas, and
                                      mineral resource extraction and transport operations be compatible with
                                      and minimize impacts on adjacent uses. (RDR)
                            NR-6: VISUAL RESOURCES
                            Goal NR-6
                            Preservation of significant visual resources that serve as scenic
                            amenities and contribute to Oakdale’s character.
                             VISUAL RESOURCES POLICIES
                            NR-6.1    Viewshed Protection. Protect views of significant visual resources within
                                      and seen from the City, such as the Stanislaus River, nearby mountains
                                      and surrounding agricultural lands. (RDR)
Also See Community Services NR-6.2    Scenic Corridor. Establish a scenic corridor along the Stanislaus River,
                   Element            and enhance public access to views along the corridor, through
                                      implementation of the Stanislaus River Corridor Access Plan. (RDR,
                                      CS-IP3)
                            NR-6.3    New Development. Require that new development be sited and
                                      designed to visually complement the natural environment, minimize
                                      impacts to scenic resources and preserve unique or special visual features
                                      through:
                       NR-14                NATURAL RESOURCES

                                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
               Creative site planning;
               Integration of natural features; and
               Appropriate scale, materials, and design to complement the
                surrounding landscape. (RDR)
NR-6.4    Lighting. Require that new lighting be designed and configured to
          minimize light pollution, glare, and spillage. (RDR)
NR-7: CULTURAL RESOURCES
Goal NR-7
Identification, protection, and enhancement of Oakdale’s important
cultural resources.
 CULTURAL RESOURCES POLICIES
NR-7.1    Preservation. Protect and preserve significant paleontological,
          archaeological, and historic resources, including those recognized at the
          national, state, and local levels. (RDR, NR-IP7, NR-IP8, NR-IP9, NR-IP10)
NR-7.2    Applicable Laws and Regulations. Ensure that local, state, and federal
          historic preservation laws, regulations, and codes are implemented.
          (RDR)
NR-7.3    Identification. Undertake programs for the identification of significant
          prehistoric, historic, paleontological, and archeological resources.
          (NR-IP11)
NR-7.4    Inclusion on Historic Registers. Promote the registration of historic
          resources in the national and state registers and in the City’s local
          inventory. (NR-IP11)
NR-7.5    Consultation. Consult with the appropriate organizations and individuals
          early in the development process (e.g., Information Centers of the
          California Historical Resources Information System, Native American
          Heritage Commission, and Native American groups and individuals) to
          minimize potential impacts to cultural resources. (RDR, IGC)
NR-7.6    Resource Assessment. Require discretionary development proposals that
          could potentially impact cultural resources to conduct a cultural resources
          survey prior to approval of new development, rehabilitation efforts, and
          remodels to ensure that potential sites are identified for avoidance or
          special treatment. (RDR, NR-IP7, NR-IP8, NR-IP9, NR-IP10)
NR-7.7    Adaptive Reuse. Encourage the preservation and adaptive reuse of
          historic sites and structures. (RDR)
                                               NATURAL RESOURCES                     NR-15

     City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
     NR-7.8    Funding and Incentives. Pursue available funding sources for cultural
               resources preservation, and consider providing financial incentives to
               private owners and development in order to maintain, rehabilitate, and
               preserve such resources. (OFB, NR-IP2)
     NR-7.9    Archaeological and Paleontological Resources. Ensure compliance with
               protocols that protect or mitigate impacts to archaeological and
               paleontological resources. (NR-IP9, NR-IP10)
     NR-7.10   Public Awareness. Work with community organizations to provide
               programs oriented to the preservation of Oakdale's history. (Existing PI)
NR-16                NATURAL RESOURCES
OAKDALE 2030 GENERAL PLAN
PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY

                                           City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                  Public Health
                                                   & Safety
The Public Health and Safety Element provides policies and programs that are
designed to protect the residents, businesses, and visitors of Oakdale from
natural and man-made disasters. The intent is to accommodate future growth as
allowed under the 2030 General Plan, while sustaining the long-term health and
safety of the community.
    Our public health and safety vision includes…
        A safe community that adequately responds in the event of
         disasters and emergencies                                             CONTENTS
        Minimized risk from potential flood and dam inundation hazards        Context
        Protection from geologic and seismic hazards                          Policy Framework
        Safe use and transport of hazardous materials                         PHS-1 Disaster Preparedness and
                                                                                       Emergency Response
                                                                               PHS-2 Flood Protection
                                                                               PHS-3 Geologic and Seismic
                                                                                       Hazards
                                                                               PHS-4 Hazardous Materials
                                        PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY                PHS-1

     City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
       Context
     The City of Oakdale is committed to sustaining the long-term health and safety of
     the community through protection from natural and man-made disasters. A
     healthy and safe Oakdale contributes to the well-being of residents, and is an
     important consideration in retaining and attracting quality businesses. Key topics
     addressed by this element include:
        Disaster Preparedness & Emergency Response – The Oakdale Fire
         Department and Oakdale Police Department provide first response to the
         City in the event of disasters and emergencies. Both Departments have
         mutual and automatic aid agreements with Stanislaus County, neighboring
         agencies, and surrounding jurisdictions. In addition, the City participates in
         the Stanislaus County Multi-Jurisdictional Hazard Mitigation Plan, which
         identifies risks posed by disasters and ways to minimize damage from those
         disasters. Oakdale periodically conducts disaster preparedness exercises to
         test and improve emergency response.
        Flood Protection – The entirety of the Stanislaus River channel within
         Oakdale contains 100-year flood and 500-year flood zones, per the
         Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) Flood Insurance Rate
         Maps (FIRM), as illustrated on Figure PHS-1. A 100-year event is defined as
         a flood that has a one percent chance of annual occurrence, and a 500-
         year event has a 0.2 percent chance of annual occurrence. Flooding along
         the Stanislaus River is largely mitigated by the New Melones Reservoir, the
         operation of which effectively limits downstream releases of water.
PHS-2                  PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY

                                           City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
Figure PHS-1 identifies FEMA Flood Zones, Awareness Floodplains, and
Designated Floodways within the Planning Area:
    FEMA Flood Zones. Key FEMA regulated flood zone areas include Zones
     A and AE, both of which require mandatory flood insurance purchase
     and application of floodplain management standards. Zone A includes
     areas subject to 100-year flood events generally determined using
     approximate methodologies. Because detailed hydraulic analyses have
     not been performed, no Base Flood Elevations (BFEs) or flood depths are
     available. Zone AE also includes areas subject to 100-year flood events,
     but as determined by detailed methods. Therefore, identified BFE’s and
     flood depths are available.
    Awareness Floodplains. Awareness floodplains are generated by the
     California Department of Water Resources, and are intended to identify
     100-year flood hazards currently not mapped as a FEMA regulated
     floodplain. The intent of awareness floodplain information is to provide an
     additional tool in understanding potential flood hazards. The awareness
     maps identify the 100-year flood hazard areas using approximate
     assessment procedures, and are simply shown as flood prone areas without
     specific depths and other flood hazard data.
    Designated Floodways. Designated floodways include the channel of the
     Stanislaus River and the adjacent land areas that would be under water
     during a flood. Designated floodways are to be maintained in order to
     discharge the base flood without cumulatively increasing the water surface
     elevation more than a designated height. Oakdale is required to regulate
     development in these floodways to ensure that there are no increases in
     upstream flood elevations, and obtain an encroachment permit from the
     Central Valley Flood Protection Board if a project is within 300 feet of a
     designated floodway.
Other information regarding flood hazards including data from the US Army
Corps of Engineers, Levee Flood Protection Zones, and historical data was either
not available or not applicable to the City of Oakdale. State regulations require
200-year flood protection in Oakdale, and other urban areas within the Central
Valley, within three years after adoption of the Central Valley Flood Protection
Plan. That Plan is anticipated to be adopted in July 2012. 200-year floodplains
have a 0.5 percent chance of annual occurrence of flooding, and have been
delineated for some regions of the Central Valley. At the time of General Plan
adoption, the lower Stanislaus River had not yet been delineated by the State
Department of Water Resources.
Two major dams, Tulloch and New Melones, are located upstream of the City. In
the rare event of dam failure, Oakdale would be inundated with water. As
reflected on Figure PHS-2, the northern portion of the City is located within the
Tulloch Dam inundation area, while the majority of the City is within the New
Melones Dam inundation area.

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               Figure PHS-2
     City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
        Geologic & Seismic Hazards – Oakdale’s topography varies, but is
         generally flat with relatively steep slopes along the Stanislaus River. Several
         soil types can be found in the City, some of which could cause geologic
         hazards associated with erosion and expansive soils.
         Although Oakdale is located in a region (within 100 kilometers) that is
         subject to seismic activity from a number of faults, no active or potentially
         active faults are known to underlie the City itself. Oakdale is not located
         within an Alquist-Priolo Earthquake Fault Zone, and no surface evidence of
         faulting has been observed. However, in the event of an earthquake in the
         region, groundshaking could affect the City and potentially cause property
         damage.
        Hazardous Materials – Hazardous materials are routinely used, stored, and
         transported into and out of Oakdale. These materials are associated with
         industrial and commercial uses, as well as educational facilities, hospitals,
         medical/dental facilities, residential uses, and agriculture. Another major
         source of hazardous materials in the City includes underground fuel tanks,
         which are primarily associated with retail gasoline stations. A number of
         federal, State, and local laws regulate the management of hazardous
         materials.
         In the event of the release of a hazardous material into the environment, the
         Oakdale Fire Department is responsible for the containment and clean-up of
         small scale releases. In the event of a large hazardous materials incident, the
         Stanislaus County Department of Environmental Resources would assist.
       Policy Framework
     PHS-1: DISASTER PREPAREDNESS AND
                     EMERGENCY RESPONSE
     Goal PHS-1
     Adequate community response in the event of disasters and
     emergencies.
      DISASTER PREPAREDNESS AND EMERGENCY RESPONSE POLICIES
     PHS-1.1    Emergency Services Planning. Maintain and improve emergency
                services planning within the City and adjacent areas. (IGC, PHS-IP1,
                PHS-IP2)
     PHS-1.2    Multi-Jurisdictional Hazard Plan. Continue to participate in, and ensure
                that new development and infrastructure are consistent with, the
PHS-6                 PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY

                                            City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
        Stanislaus County Multi-Jurisdictional Hazard Mitigation Plan. (RDR, MP,
        IGC, PHS-IP1)
PHS-1.3 Emergency and Disaster-Preparedness. Coordinate with Stanislaus
        County and other applicable agencies in conducting disaster-
        preparedness exercises to periodically test and improve emergency
        response. (IGC, PHS-IP1)
PHS-1.4 Evacuation Routes. Regularly review and update as needed, the
        adequacy of evacuation routes in the event of an emergency. (PHS-IP1)
PHS-1.5 Critical Facilities. Plan for the continued function of critical facilities such
        as hospitals, fire stations, and emergency command centers following a
        major disaster to facilitate post-disaster recovery. Locate such facilities
        outside of identified hazard areas. (PHS-IP1)
PHS-1.6 Emergency Access. Require adequate road standards, driveway widths
        and clearances around structures consistent with local and State
        requirements to ensure emergency access. (RDR, MP)
PHS-1.7 Fire Flow Demands. Provide sufficient water storage and infrastructure to          Also See Public Facilities Element
        meet emergency fire flow demands. (MP)
PHS-2: FLOOD PROTECTION
Goal PHS-2
Minimized risk to lives and property posed by potential flood and
dam inundation hazards.
 FLOOD PROTECTION POLICIES
PHS-2.1 National Flood Insurance Program. Continue to participate in the
        National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP) to maintain the City’s eligibility
        for flood insurance. (OFB, IGC, PHS-IP2)
PHS-2.2 Minimize Flooding Risk. Require a minimum 100-year flood protection
        and regulate development in accordance with local, state, and federal
        requirements to avoid or minimize the risk of flood damage. (RDR, MP,
        PHS-IP2)
PHS-2.3 Central Valley Flood Protection Plan. Require new development, within
        three years after adoption of the Central Valley Flood Protection Plan, to
        provide 200-year flood protection in accordance with state regulations.
        (RDR, MP, PHS-IP2, PHS-IP3)
PHS-2.4 Development within Flood Hazard Zones. Encourage new development
        to not build within a flood hazard zone as defined by FEMA. If such
                                          PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY                        PHS-7

                            City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                      development is approved, ensure that it is constructed in accordance with
                                      city, state, and federal regulations (e.g. NFIP) to minimize flood damage.
                                      (RDR)
                                        FLOOD HAZARD ZONES
                                         Flood hazard zones are designated by the Federal Emergency Management
                                         Agency (FEMA) on the Flood Insurance Rate Maps (FIRM), and include both 100-
                                         year and 500-year floodplains. A 100-year event is defined as a flood that has
                                         one percent chance of annual occurrence and a 500-year has a 0.2 percent
                                         chance of annual occurrence.
                            PHS-2.5   Development within Dam Inundation Areas. Require new development
                                      located within identified dam inundation areas to be designed to
                                      minimize potential flood damage from dam failure to the extent feasible.
                                      (RDR)
Also See Community Services PHS-2.6   Kerr Park. Maintain the Kerr Park floodplain in a natural state as a
                   Element            nature discovery park that connects to the Stanley Wakefield Wilderness
                                      Area. (MP, OFB).
                            PHS-2.7   Agency Coordination. Coordinate efforts with local, regional, state, and
                                      federal agencies to minimize flood hazards and improve flood
                                      protection. (IGC, PHS-IP2)
                            PHS-3: GEOLOGIC AND SEISMIC HAZARDS
                            Goal PHS-3
                            Residents, properties, and critical facilities protected from geologic
                            and seismic hazards.
                             GEOLOGIC AND SEISMIC HAZARD POLICIES
                            PHS-3.1   Safety Standards. Regularly review and enforce the seismic and geologic
                                      safety standards included in the Uniform Building Code. (RDR)
                            PHS-3.2   Existing Structure Retrofit. Encourage the upgrade, retrofit, and/or
                                      relocation of critical facilities (e.g., hospitals, fire stations, police stations,
                                      etc.) and other structures that do not meet current building and safety
                                      code standards. (RDR, MP, JP, PHS-IP2)
                            PHS-3.3   Geotechnical Studies. Require that a geotechnical study be prepared by
                                      a certified geotechnical engineer recommending measures to avoid or
                                      minimize risks for development in areas where geologic or seismic
                                      hazards may be present. (RDR)
                       PHS-8                 PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY
                                             City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
PHS-4: HAZARDOUS MATERIALS
Goal PHS-4
The safe production, use, storage, disposal, and transport of
hazardous materials.
 HAZARDOUS MATERIALS POLICIES
PHS-4.1 Hazardous Materials Regulation. Coordinate with Stanislaus County and
        other applicable agencies to enforce pertinent laws, disclosure and siting
        requirements that regulate the production, use, storage, disposal, and
        transport of hazardous materials. Provide appropriate notification in the
        event of a violation. (RDR, OFB, IGC, PHS-IP2)
PHS-4.2 Site Identification. Participate in efforts to identify sites previously used for
        hazardous materials storage and disposal. (RDR, OFB)
PHS-4.3 Known Areas of Contamination. Require new development in known
        contamination areas to perform comprehensive soil and groundwater
        contamination assessments. If contamination exceeds regulatory levels,
        require remediation procedures consistent with county, regional, and
        State regulations prior to any site disturbance or development. (RDR)
PHS-4.4 Best Practices. Encourage industries, businesses and residents to utilize
        best practices and technologies that reduce the use of hazardous
        materials and generation of hazardous wastes. (RDR, JP, PI)
PHS-4.5 Hazardous Materials Disposal. Continue to work with Stanislaus County
        to encourage homeowners to dispose of household hazardous waste and
        E-waste at special collection events and at the County’s collection center.
        (IGC, PI)
PHS-4.6 Education. Promote public education efforts regarding the proper use,
        storage, and disposal of hazardous materials. (PI)
PHS-4.7 City Truck Routes. Coordinate with the State and other appropriate                     Also See Mobility Element
        agencies to update truck routes on City roadways and State highways to
        continue to minimize the transport of hazardous materials through
        residential and other sensitive land use areas. (IGC, M-IP6)
                                          PUBLIC HEALTH & SAFETY                         PHS-9


OAKDALE 2030 GENERAL PLAN
NOISE

                                            City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                                                               Noise
The Noise Element presents a set of goals, policies and standards to ensure that
exposure to harmful noise is minimized in Oakdale. It is the intent of this element to
make certain that development allowed under the 2030 General Plan will be
compatible with the existing and future noise environment, and diminish potential
exposure to excessive or harmful noise.
    Our noise vision includes…
      Minimized exposure to excessive noise and vibration
      Land uses compatible with the existing and future noise
       environment
      Protection of noise-sensitive land uses
      Establishment of consistent noise standards
                                                                                       CONTENTS
                                                                                       Context
                                                                                       Policy Framework
                                                                                       N-1     Noise Regulation
                                                             NOISE                    N-1

   City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
     Context
   The City of Oakdale recognizes the relationship between noise and the well-being
   of the community. Excessive noise levels can affect the physical health, property
   values, and economic productivity of Oakdale’s residents, businesses, and visitors.
   As such, regulating noise is essential to creating a safe, compatible, and productive
   environment.
   Noise sources are generally classified in one of two major categories:
   stationary/non-transportation sources; or mobile/transportation sources. A
   stationary noise source includes fixed equipment such as HVAC or heavy industrial
   equipment. Mobile/transportation noise sources can be generated from traffic,
   trains, and aircraft.
       Traffic Noise. Throughout Oakdale, the primary noise sources is and will
        continue to be transportation related. Vehicle traffic along SR 120 and SR 108
        are the greatest noise source, and cause sustained noise levels. Existing
        roadway noise exposure and contour distances in Oakdale are presented in
        Table N-1. Future roadway noise exposure and contour distances based on
        development allowed under the 2030 General Plan are presented in Table N-
        2. At the time of this General Plan’s approval, a final alignment for the NCC
        had not been adopted. Should an alignment be adopted that generates noise
        within the Planning Area, the policies in this element will be applied.
       Aircraft Noise. The Oakdale Municipal Airport is an “island” extension of the
        City limits, located over 1 mile to the southeast of the City. Future development
        under the 2030 General Plan will be consistent with the Airport Land Use
        Commission Plan (ALUCP) as was being updated by the County at the time of
N-2                    NOISE

                                                      City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
      General Plan approval. Based upon information generated for the ALUCP
      update, no conflicts between airport operations and the City’s noise regulations
      were identified. Existing and future airport noise contours are shown in Figure
      N-1. It is anticipated that future airport operations will be similar to existing
      operations and minimal changes in noise contours would occur.
     Rail Line Noise. The City of Oakdale is served by four rail lines: the Burlington
      Northern and Santa Fe (BNSF) Railroad, the Union Pacific Railroad (UPRR), the
      Oakdale Traction Corporation (OTC), and the Sierra Railroad. Estimated
      existing and future rail line noise exposure and contour distances are presented
      in Table N-3. As shown in Table N-3, train operations are not considered to be
      a dominant source of noise within the City.
     Stationary Sources. Stationary noise sources also contribute to the ambient
      noise environment in Oakdale. Residential areas can generate noise through
      the use of heating and cooling equipment, and through landscape maintenance
      activities such as gasoline-powered lawnmowers. Commercial uses can
      generate noise through the operation of rooftop heating and cooling
      equipment, and other activities, such as trash collection, and deliveries.
      Stationary noise sources at industrial uses include shipping and loading
      facilities, as well as large-scale manufacturing and processing equipment.
      Outdoor sports facilities that attract large numbers of spectators, such as high
      school football fields, can produce noise that affects nearby receptors.
  NOISE DEFINITIONS
  Decibel (dB): A logarithmic unit of sound intensity where 0 dB is the    Maximum Sound Level (Lmax): The Lmax is the highest instantaneous
  threshold of normal hearing and 130 dB is the threshold of pain.         sound level measured during a specified period.
  Decibel (dBA): Measurement unit for A-weighted decibels, which are       Day-Night Average Level (Ldn): The Ldn is the energy-average of A-
  commonly used for measuring environmental and industrial noise and       weighted sound levels occurring over a 24-hour period, with a 10 dB
  the potential hearing damage associated with noise health effects.       penalty applied to A-weighted sound levels occurring during nighttime
                                                                           hours (10 p.m.-7 a.m.). The Ldn is often noted as the DNL.
  Equivalent Sound Level (Leq): The Leq represents an average of the
  sound energy occurring over a specified time period. In effect, the Leq  Community Noise Equivalent Level (CNEL): Similar to Ldn, CNEL is the
  is the steady-state sound level containing the same acoustical energy    energy-average of the A-weighted sound levels occurring over a 24-
  as the time-varying sound that actually occurs during the same period.   hour period, with a 10 dB penalty applied to A-weighted sound levels
  The 1-hour, A-weighted equivalent sound level (Leq[h]) is the energy     occurring during the nighttime hours (10 p.m.-7 a.m.), and a 5 dB
  average of A-weighted sound levels occurring during a 1-hour period,     penalty applied to the A-weighted sound levels occurring during
  and is the basis for noise abatement criteria (NAC) used by Caltrans     evening hours (7 p.m.-10 p.m.). The CNEL is usually within 1 dB of the
  and the FHWA.                                                            Ldn, and for all intents and purposes, the two are interchangeable. As
                                                                           it is easier to compute and of more common use, the Ldn is used as the
  Percentile-Exceeded Sound Level (Ln): The Ln represents the sound
                                                                           long-term noise measure by the City.
  level exceeded “n” percentage of a specified period (e.g., L10 is the
  sound level exceeded 10% of the time, and L90 is the sound level
  exceeded 90% of the time).

  Policy Framework
N-1: NOISE REGULATION
Goal N-1
Minimal exposure of residents and businesses to harmful noise and
vibrations.
 NOISE AND LAND USE COMPATIBILITY POLICIES
N-1.1         Land Use Compatibility. Consider the compatibility of new developments
              with the existing noise environment when reviewing discretionary proposals.
              (RDR, N-IP1)
N 1.2         New Noise-Sensitive Development. Require development of new noise-
              sensitive land uses to mitigate noise impacts where the projected exterior or
              interior environmental noise levels appropriate to the land use types exceed
              those shown in Tables N-4 (Maximum Allowable Environmental Noise
              Standards from Transportation Sources) and/or N-5 (Noise Level Standards
              for Stationary Sources). (RDR, N-IP1)
                NOISE SENSITIVE USES
                Noise sensitive uses are defined as homes, daycares, schools, convalescent homes,
                medical facilities, and hospitals.
N 1.3         New Stationary Noise Sources. Require new stationary noise sources to
              mitigate noise impacts on noise-sensitive uses where the noise from that
              source alone exceeds the exterior levels specified in Table N-5 (Noise Level
              Standards from Stationary Sources). (RDR, N-IP1)
N 1.4         Frequent, High-Noise Events. Require development of noise-sensitive uses
              proposed in areas subject to frequent, high-noise events (such as aircraft
                                                                        NOISE                     N-7
   City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                   over flights, or train and truck traffic) to adequately evaluate and mitigate
                   the potential for noise-related impacts. Mitigation shall ensure that noise-
                   related annoyance, sleep disruption, speech interference, and other similar
                   effects are minimized using metrics and methodologies appropriate to the
                   effect(s) to be assessed and avoided. (RDR, N-IP1)
   Table N-4:         MAXIMUM ALLOWABLE ENVIRONMENTAL
                      NOISE STANDARDS – TRANSPORTATION
                      SOURCES

                                                              Standard for Outdoo             Interior

    Mobile Homes)
   Residential (Multi Family)                                          65d               45               N/A
   Transient Lodging (Motels/Hotels)                                   65  d
                                                                                         45               N/A
   Schools, Libraries, Churches, Hospitals, Nursing                     70               45               N/A
   Homes, Museums

   Playgrounds, Neighborhood Parks                                      70              N/A               N/A

   Industrial, Manufacturing, Utilities, and                            75              N/A                45
   Agriculture
   Where a proposed use is not specifically listed on this table, the use shall comply with the noise exposure
   standards for the nearest similar use as determined by the Community Development and Services Director.
   a.    Outdoor activity areas for residential developments are considered to be the back yard patios or decks
         of single-family residential units, and the patios or common areas where people generally congregate for
         multi-family development.
         Outdoor activity areas for nonresidential developments are considered to be those common areas where
         people generally congregate, including outdoor seating areas. Where the location of outdoor activity
         areas is unknown, the exterior noise standard shall be applied to the property line of the receiving land
         use.
   b.    As determined for a typical worst-case hour during periods of use.
   c.    Where it is not possible to reduce noise in outdoor activity areas to 60 dB, Ldn/CNEL or less using a
         practical application of the best-available noise reduction measures, an exterior level of up to 65 dB,
         Ldn/CNEL may be allowed provided that available exterior noise level reduction measures have been
         implemented and interior noise levels are in compliance with this table.
   d.    Where it is not possible to reduce noise in outdoor activity areas to 65 dB, Ldn/CNEL or less using a
         practical application of the best-available noise reduction measures, an exterior level of up to 70 dB,
         Ldn/CNEL may be allowed provided that available exterior noise level reduction measures have been
         implemented and interior noise levels are in compliance with this table.

                   STATIONARY SOURCES

Noise levels are measured at the property line of the noise-sensitive use.
N-1.5          Acoustical Analysis. Require preparation of an acoustical analysis as part
               of the environmental review process for proposed projects that involve
               development of noise sensitive land uses or development that has the
               potential to impact noise sensitive land uses. The acoustical analysis shall
               be conducted by qualified personnel utilizing acceptable methodologies.
               (RDR, N-IP1)
N-1.6          Mixed Use Development. Encourage new mixed use developments to locate
               potentially incompatible noise sources away from the residential portion of
               the development. (RDR)
 TRANSPORTATION-RELATED NOISE POLICIES
N-1.7          Noise-Compatible Land Uses. Encourage noise-compatible land uses along
               existing and future roadways, highways, and railroads. (RDR)
N-1.8          Mitigation Measures along Roadways. Include noise mitigation measures
               in the design of all future streets and highways, and improvements along
               existing streets and highways. Measures should emphasize the
               establishment of natural buffers or use of setbacks between roadways and
               adjoining noise sensitive uses when feasible. (RDR, MP, N-IP1, N-IP2)
N-1.9          Rail. Work with railroad operators to minimize noise levels produced by
               trains and whistle noise within the City by reducing nighttime operations
               and ensuring consistency with the noise levels shown in Table N-6
               (Groundborne Vibration Impact Criteria for General Assessment). (JP,
               N-IP1)
N-1.10         Airport Plans. Regulate development within the 65 dBA CNEL airport noise
               contour in accordance with plans adopted by the Airport Land Use
               Commission and the City. (RDR, IGC)
 NON-TRANSPORTATION RELATED NOISE POLICIES
N-1.11         Construction Noise. Minimize construction-related noise and vibration by
               limiting construction activities within 500 feet of noise-sensitive uses to
               7:00 A.M. to 6:00 P.M. on weekdays, 8:00 A.M. to 5:00 P.M. on Saturdays,
               and no construction on Sundays and holidays unless permission for the
               latter has been granted by the City. (RDR, N-IP1)

OAKDALE 2030 GENERAL PLAN
IMPLEMENTATION

                                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                             Implementation
The ultimate measure of an adopted general plan is how effectively its policies are
carried out to achieve the community’s vision and goals. The purpose of this chapter
is to describe the actions the City of Oakdale will undertake, and will require of new
developments, to achieve the city’s vision of its future. This chapter also discusses
monitoring, amending, and maintaining consistency with the General Plan.
   General Plan
   Administration
REVIEW AND MONITORING  
The City of Oakdale will regularly review the 2030 General Plan to evaluate
progress in implementing its goals and policies. Since issues the General Plan
addresses will continue to evolve over time, a regular review and reporting of
implementation will help ensure the City is moving forward in achieving the General
Plan’s vision. This review will report on the status of each implementation program,
                                                    IMPLEMENTATION                    IM-1

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
    and consider any new planning tools, policy approaches, funding sources, and
    feedback from monitoring activities. The findings of the review will be sent to the
    Governor’s Office of Planning and Research, as required by Government Code
    Section 65400.
    GENERAL PLAN AMENDMENTS  
    As conditions and needs change, the City may want to consider proposed
    amendments to the General Plan. Some of these amendments may consist of
    changes to the Land Use Diagram, while others may include or consist of policy
    changes. Each of these changes will need to be carefully evaluated for merit,
    potential impacts, and for consistency with the remainder of the General Plan. State
    law requires that the General Plan be an integrated and internally consistent set of
    goals, policies, and implementation programs.
    State law also limits the number of times per year that a general law city, such as
    Oakdale, can amend mandatory elements of the General Plan. An element may not
    be amended more than four times in a one calendar year except in certain
    circumstances as described in Government Code Section 65358. Each amendment
    may include more than one change to the General Plan. All proposed General Plan
    Amendments are to be processed consistent with the City’s standard review
    requirements.
    GENERAL PLAN CONSISTENCY  
    The City of Oakdale will use the General Plan to guide a wide range of actions. All
    actions and decisions made by the City should be consistent with the adopted
    General Plan to ensure that its policies are systematically implemented. City actions
    that must be consistent with the General Plan include, but are not limited to: master
    plans; capital projects; subdivision approvals; development code and zoning;
    specific plans; development projects; and development agreements.
      Implementation Tools and
      Programs
    The City will implement a majority of the 2030 General Plan’s goals and policies
    through a number of routine actions, regulations, and operations. These “Standard
    Implementation Tools” can be grouped into the following six categories:
         1. City Regulations and Development Review;
         2. City Master Plans, Programs and Other Documents;
         3. City Operations, Financing and Budget;
         4. Intergovernmental Coordination;
IM-2                  IMPLEMENTATION

                                              City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
     5. Joint Partnerships; and
     6. Public Information
Where a particular policy is not implemented, or fully implemented, by the standard
actions or tools above, “Specific Implementation Programs” have been identified.
The Specific Implementation Programs are focused actions to implement individual
policies or a series of related policies. Each Specific Implementation Program
includes identification of City departments responsible for implementation. Timing of
Implementation Programs will be determined by the City based upon the availability
of funding and prioritization of resources.
Every policy within the 2030 General Plan is linked to one or more implementation
tool or program. Two- to three-letter identifiers (italicized and in parentheses) are
shown after each policy, indicating the tools or programs that will implement the
policy.
STANDARD IMPLEMENTATION TOOLS  
City Regulations and Development Review (RDR)
The City’s Zoning Code is one of the primary tool for implementing the General
Plan. The Zoning Code provides permitted uses, development standards, and other
regulations that direct development and support implementation of General Plan
policies. In addition to the Zoning Code, there are other City regulations, plans and
policies in place to ensure growth and change occur in a consistent manner that
furthers the direction of the General Plan. The City’s Zoning Code and other
regulations also establish development review processes that provide for City review
of individual project proposals and authorize the City to approve, deny, or
condition projects based on their consistency with the General Plan and other
considerations.
Regulatory plans and ordinances that will commonly be used by the City of
Oakdale to implement General Plan policies include, but are not limited to:
          Zoning Code (and other chapters of the City’s Municipal Code)
          Specific Plans
          Subdivision Ordinance
          Building and Safety Codes
          Development Review
          Design Expectations
          City Standard Specifications
          California Environmental Quality Act
Subsequent to adoption of the General Plan, the City will review and update its
regulatory plans, ordinances, and processes, as appropriate, to be consistent with
and further implement the 2030 General Plan and associated Climate Action Plan.
                                                  IMPLEMENTATION                     IM-3

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
    Immediate priority should be given to updating the City’s Zoning Code and
    implementing the financing plans for CCSP and SPSP.
    City Master Plans, Programs, and Other Documents (MP)
    Oakdale has adopted various master plans, programs, and other documents that
    direct City services and facilities. Key amongst these is the City’s Capital
    Improvement Program which is the primary mechanism to schedule and fund
    improvements of citywide benefit. Master plans, programs, and other documents
    that will commonly be used by the City of Oakdale to implement the General Plan
    include, but are not limited to:
              Capital Improvement Program (within the Capital Facilities Fee Updated
               Nexus Study)
              Oakdale Municipal Airport Master Plan
              Urban Water Management Plan
              Sewer Master Plan
              Storm Drainage Study
              Storm Water Management Program
              Fire Master Plan
              Stanislaus County Multi-Jurisdictional Hazard Mitigation Plan
              Open Space, Recreation, and Conservation Master Plan
              Bicycle and Pedestrian Master Plan
              Stanislaus County Non-Motorized Transportation Plan
              Climate Action Plan
              Oakdale-Riverbank Corridor Area Agreement
              Oakdale Enterprise Zone
    Subsequent to adoption of the General Plan, the City will review and update its
    master plans, programs, and other documents, as appropriate, to be consistent with
    and further implement the 2030 General Plan and associated Climate Action Plan.
    Immediate priority should be given to creating a long-term Capital Improvement
    Program, updating the Capital Facilities Fee, and updating the utility master
    plans/studies/programs.
    City Operations, Financing and Budget (OFB)
    The City provides a broad range of services to its residents, businesses, and visitors
    and manages and operates public facilities to meet community needs. The type,
    quantity and quality of services and facilities provided by the City should account
    for General Plan policy, and can make a significant difference in how effectively the
    General Plan is implemented. Services and facilities require financial resources from
    a variety of sources. The City’s projected revenues and recommended spending are
    accounted for in its annual budget.
IM-4                  IMPLEMENTATION

                                               City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
The following are some of the revenue sources that have been used by or are
available to the City of Oakdale to support development, maintenance, or operation
of public facilities and services consistent with the General Plan:
       Property tax revenue
       Sales tax revenue
       User fees
       Capital Facilities Fee/Development fees
       Quimby Act (Park) dedications
       School impact fees
       County impact fees
       Business improvement districts
       Community facilities and special assessment districts
       Municipal bonds
       Special taxes
       County, state, and federal funding
Subsequent to adoption of the General Plan, the City will review and update its fee
and other revenue generating programs, to be consistent with and further
implement the services, facilities and programs identified in the 2030 General Plan
and associated Climate Action Plan.
Intergovernmental Coordination (IGC)
For a number of policies, implementation of the General Plan will depend upon or
be enhanced through coordination with and potential actions by other agencies.
Decisions made by the City affect the region, and activities outside of Oakdale have
varying impacts on the City. Implementing General Plan policies necessitates
intergovernmental coordination and collaboration in order to achieve wide-ranging
goals. The City must coordinate with numerous local, regional, state, and federal
agencies that provide services, facilities, funding and/or administer regulations that
directly or indirectly affect General Plan implementation.
Public agencies that the City of Oakdale will commonly need to coordinate with to
implement General Plan policies include, but are not limited to:
           Local agencies such as Stanislaus County; City of Riverbank; City of
            Modesto; special districts; and school districts
           Regional agencies such as Stanislaus County Local Agency Formation
            Commission (LAFCO); San Joaquin Valley Air Pollution Control District;
            Regional Water Quality Control Board; Stanislaus Council of
            Governments (StanCOG); and Stanislaus County Airport Land Use
            Commission
                                                    IMPLEMENTATION                    IM-5

    City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
                State agencies such as Caltrans and Native American Heritage
                 Commission (NAHC)
                Federal agencies such as U.S. Fish and Wildlife Services (USFWS); U.S.
                 Army Corps of Engineers; and Federal Emergency Management Agency
                 (FEMA)
    Joint Partnerships (JP)
    Partnering with non-governmental public and private organizations provides
    additional opportunities to implement the General Plan in an effective and efficient
    manner. A coordinated approach to addressing various General Plan policies with
    agencies and organizations that have expertise in specific areas will allow Oakdale
    to better serve its residents. Non-governmental agencies and organizations that the
    City may coordinate and partner with include, but are not limited to, utility
    companies, transit providers, solid waste services, private schools, higher education
    institutions, healthcare providers/hospitals, railroad operators, chamber of
    commerce, development interests, and businesses.
    Public Information (PI)
    The City can use a wide range of tools to keep Oakdale residents informed of City
    services, activities and issues that directly relate to implementation of General Plan
    policies. The City of Oakdale may distribute public information through media such
    as brochures, pamphlets, the city’s website, workshops, seminars, public access
    television, radio, newspapers, public hearings, neighborhood and community
    meetings, customer service hotlines, and similar.

     Public Facilities
     PF-1P1    Pursue available state, federal and other funding sources to support the
               planning, improvement, operations and maintenance of water, sewer and
               storm drainage facilities.
               Implements Policy(ies): PF-1.2, PF-2.2, and PF-3.2
               Responsible Department: Public Works
     PF-IP2    Continue to prepare an annual report on the quality and quantity of
               groundwater.
               Implements Policy(ies): PF-1.6
               Responsible Department: Public Works
     PF-IP3    Continue to work with surrounding jurisdictions, Stanislaus County, the
               Oakdale Irrigation District, the Modesto Irrigation District, and other
               applicable agencies to prepare a regional groundwater management plan
               for the East San Joaquin Groundwater Subbasin, and regularly review and
               update the Integrated Regional Groundwater Management Plan for the
               Modesto Subbasin to protect groundwater quality and prevent overdraft
               conditions. These plans shall identify potential groundwater recharge
               opportunities to offset projected reductions in groundwater recharge
               associated with planned increases in impervious surface coverage.
               Recharge opportunities identified by the plan shall include, but not be
               limited to, infiltration basins and other groundwater recharge areas. The
               plan shall recommend recharge areas and proposed infrastructure, as well
               as a proposed implementation schedule.
               Implements Policy(ies): PF-1.8 and NR-4.2
               Responsible Department: Public Works
     Community Services
     CS-1P1    Pursue available state, federal and other funding sources to support
               facilities, equipment, programs and staffing for police, fire, parks and
               recreation.
               Implements Policy(ies): CS-1.1, CS-2.1 and CS-3.18
               Responsible Department: Police, Fire, Community Development & Services
     CS-IP2    Prepare, adopt, and regularly update a Police Master Plan.

        transfer of development rights, land dedication, or acquisition by the City or

        Responsible Department: Community Development & Services

        space acquisition, management, maintenance and restoration; agricultural
        land preservation and mitigation; activities and programs that reduce air
        quality and greenhouse gas emissions; groundwater and surface water
        management; and the preservation of paleontological, archeological, and
        historical resources.

        Responsible Department: Community Development & Services, Public
        Works
NR-IP3  Prepare and adopt a Plan for Agricultural Preservation for any projects
        involving adoption of a new Specific Plan or annexation/Sphere of
        Influence modification consistent with the Stanislaus LAFCO Agricultural
        Preservation Policy. Such a Plan shall include: a detailed analysis of direct
        and indirect impacts to agricultural resources on the site and surrounding
        area, including a detailed description of the agricultural resources affected
        and information regarding Williamson Act Lands; a vacant land inventory
        and absorption study evaluating lands within the existing boundaries of the
        jurisdiction that could be developed for the same or similar uses; existing
        and proposed densities (persons per acre); relevant County and City
        General Plan policies and specific plans; consistency with regional planning

               efforts; and an analysis of mitigation measures that could offset impacts to

IM-12                 IMPLEMENTATION

                                              City of Oakdale 2030 General Plan
NR-IP9  Require an archaeological resource investigation for projects subject to
        discretionary approval which involve any ground disturbance, to be
        prepared by an archaeologist that meets the Secretary of Interior’s
        professional qualifications standards. As determined necessary by the
        archaeologist and the City, the investigation may include, but may not be
        limited to, a records search, pre-construction field surveys, research, and
        testing, and/or other methods that identify whether a substantial adverse
        impact on significant archaeological resource would occur. If archaeological
        resources are discovered, the archaeologist and the City will consult to
        determine the appropriate next step(s).
        Implements Policy(ies): NR-7.1, NR-7.6 and NR-7.9
        Responsible Department: Community Development and Services
NR-IP10 Require that when any subsurface cultural resources, paleontological
        resources, or human remains are encountered, all work within 100 feet of
        the discovery be stopped and the area protected from further disturbance
        until the discovery is evaluated by a qualified professional. The appropriate
        City personnel shall be notified immediately. The resources shall be
        examined by qualified personnel to determine their significance and
        develop appropriate protection and preservation measures, if necessary. If
        human remains are discovered, they shall be treated in compliance with
        applicable state and federal laws, including notifying the County Coroner
        and consulting with the California Native American Heritage Commission,
        as appropriate.
        Implements Policy(ies): NR-7.1, NR-7.6 and NR-7.9
        Responsible Department: Community Development and Services
NR-IP11 Develop a process and schedule to update the survey previously undertaken
        for the City in order to identify significant cultural resources in Oakdale, and
        promote the registration of those resources on the national and state
        registers and local inventory.
        Implements Policy(ies): NR-7.3, and NR-7.4
        Responsible Department: Community Development and Services
